% ==========================================================================
%  Chapter 88 -- Validation Reboot Master Plan
% ==========================================================================

\chapter{Validation Reboot Master Plan}
\label{ch:validation-reboot-master-plan}

\paragraph{Normative status.}
This chapter defines the validation program that shall replace the current
legacy mixture of exploratory drivers, partial regression surfaces, and
large executables that do not yet provide a scientifically clean entry point.
Its purpose is methodological before it is numerical: to prevent the library
from inheriting validation authority from surfaces that were never designed as
controlled benchmarks.

\section{Why the validation campaign must restart from zero}

The library already contains many tests and several large validation-oriented
drivers.  That is valuable, but not sufficient.  A test only proves what it
actually constrains, and a driver only validates what its inputs, outputs, and
acceptance criteria make explicit.  If those criteria are weak, hidden, or
historically accidental, the resulting evidence cannot be promoted to a
scientific claim without re-audit.

The new validation program therefore adopts the following rule:
\begin{equation}
  \text{claim}
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  \text{computational artifact}
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  \text{audited evidence}
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  \text{acceptance gate}.
\end{equation}
The campaign is not allowed to skip any arrow in this chain.

This rule follows directly from the continuum and finite-element structure
already fixed elsewhere in the project.  The mechanical object is defined in
terms of configuration, work-conjugate pairs, and history variables; the
discrete object is defined in terms of residual, tangent, and incremental state
commitment; and the validation object must therefore be defined in terms of a
traceable relation between those theoretical statements and reproducible
numerical evidence.  See, in particular,
\cite{BonetWood2008,Crisfield1991_NLFEA_Vol1,DeBorst2012_NonlinearFEM}.

\section{Legacy quarantine policy}

The restart does \emph{not} imply immediate destructive deletion.  Current
surfaces remain useful as audited input, but they are no longer allowed to act
as normative validation anchors until the replacement baseline exists.

\begin{table}[htbp]
  \centering
  \caption{Legacy validation surfaces during the reboot.}
  \label{tab:validation-legacy-policy}
  \small
  \begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.30\textwidth}p{0.23\textwidth}p{0.37\textwidth}@{}}
    \toprule
    \textbf{Legacy surface} & \textbf{Temporary status} & \textbf{Disposition rule} \\
    \midrule
    \texttt{src/validation/ComprehensiveCyclicValidation.cpp}
    & audited input only
    & keep available for provenance; quarantine to \texttt{.old} only after the
      new single-column baseline is operational. \\

    \texttt{src/validation/TableCyclicValidationStructural.cpp}
    & audited input only
    & useful as seed data because it already traverses beam columns from
      \(N=2\) to \(N=10\), but it may not act as validated truth. \\

    \texttt{doc/ch82\_cyclic\_validation.tex} and
    \texttt{doc/ch85\_comprehensive\_cyclic\_multiscale\_validation.tex}
    & historical record
    & preserve as provenance; do not present as the normative validation
      narrative once the rebooted campaign is in place. \\
    \bottomrule
  \end{tabular}
\end{table}

\section{First scientific target}

The first normative target is deliberately narrow:
\begin{quote}
  \emph{a single reinforced-concrete rectangular column subjected to
  progressively amplified cyclic lateral displacement up to approximately
  \(50\) to \(100\) mm, with optional axial compression, first in one lateral
  direction and later, if justified, in two directions.}
\end{quote}

This target is small enough to be inspectable, rich enough to expose section
nonlinearity, hysteresis, stiffness degradation, and eventually crack-driven
continuum effects, and disciplined enough to support direct comparison between
reduced structural models and full continuum models.

\section{Canonical campaign phases}

The new campaign is frozen in code through
\texttt{src/validation/ValidationCampaignCatalog.hh}.  Table
\ref{tab:validation-reboot-phases} summarizes the representative workstreams.

\begin{table}[htbp]
  \centering
  \caption{Canonical validation reboot workstreams.}
  \label{tab:validation-reboot-phases}
  \scriptsize
  \setlength{\tabcolsep}{3pt}
  \begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{@{}p{0.18\textwidth}p{0.12\textwidth}p{0.14\textwidth}p{0.25\textwidth}X@{}}
    \toprule
    \textbf{Workstream} & \textbf{Phase} & \textbf{Priority} &
    \textbf{Primary objective} & \textbf{Gate impact} \\
    \midrule
    Governance reset and evidence protocol
    & 0 & mandatory
    & Freeze the rule that legacy surfaces may inform the campaign but cannot
      anchor validation without re-audit.
    & Blocks every later gate. \\

    Formulation and solver scope audit
    & 1 & mandatory
    & Re-audit TL, UL, corotational, Newton, dynamics, and continuation as
      computational slices.
    & Blocks structural, continuum, and escalation stages. \\

    Uniaxial material and section baseline
    & 2 & mandatory
    & Re-audit steel, concrete, and fiber-section ingredients before using them
      in the reference column.
    & Blocks both reduced and continuum column campaigns. \\

    Reduced-order RC column matrix
    & 3 & mandatory
    & Validate the rectangular column with Timoshenko beam models from
      \(N=2\) to \(N=10\), including hysteresis and moment-curvature outputs.
    & First structural acceptance gate. \\

    Beam integration family extension
    & 3 & mandatory
    & Replace the current one-rule beam integration path with an explicit
      Gauss/Lobatto/Radau strategy family.
    & Required before the structural column campaign can close honestly. \\

    Continuum RC column matrix
    & 4 & mandatory
    & Build the equivalent 3D continuum column with Hex8/20/27 and consistent
      top-face displacement control.
    & Blocks continuum closure and escalation. \\

    Reduced-versus-continuum equivalence
    & 5 & mandatory
    & Quantify agreement in stiffness, strength, dissipation, and loop shape
      before reopening larger structural examples.
    & Final gate before large structures. \\

    Reinforcement discretization extension
    & 4 & conditional
    & Introduce \texttt{TrussElement<Nnodes>} or an equivalent richer
      reinforcement carrier only if the bonded 2-node path proves insufficient.
    & Does not block the first campaign by default. \\

    Alternative concrete model extension
    & 2 & conditional
    & Add other concrete models only if the audited campaign shows that current
      uniaxial or continuum concrete paths are not sufficient.
    & Evidence-driven, not promise-driven. \\

    Force-based structural element path
    & 6 & deferred
    & Open a later growth track toward flexibility-based/force-based elements.
    & Valuable, but intentionally non-blocking for the first column baseline. \\
    \bottomrule
  \end{tabularx}
\end{table}

\section{Beam-axis quadrature family as a structural validation enabler}

One concrete blocker identified during the reboot is subtle but important:
for a section-based beam formulation, the axial quadrature rule is not merely
an integration detail. It also defines the \emph{section stations} at which
constitutive history lives and, for the current mixed Timoshenko formulation,
the tying stations used by the reduced shear field. Changing the beam-axis rule
therefore changes both
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the accuracy of the element integral, and
  \item the discrete placement of sectional history.
\end{enumerate}
This is precisely why the reboot could not honestly validate a rectangular RC
column while the beam path remained nominally tied to one quadrature family.

The library now exposes an explicit compile-time beam-axis quadrature family in
\texttt{src/numerics/numerical\_integration/BeamAxisQuadrature.hh}.  The
current family includes:
\begin{itemize}
  \item Gauss--Legendre rules, exact for polynomials up to degree
    \(2m-1\) with \(m\) stations;
  \item Gauss--Lobatto rules, endpoint-inclusive and exact up to degree
    \(2m-3\);
  \item Gauss--Radau rules, single-endpoint-inclusive and exact up to degree
    \(2m-2\).
\end{itemize}
These exactness properties are classical
\cite{Crisfield1991_NLFEA_Vol1,bathe2014_FiniteElementProcedures} and matter
here because the reduced-column campaign explicitly compares section-placement
families as part of the model, not as a hidden numerical afterthought.

For the degenerate one-station case (\(m=1\)), used by the 2-node beam family,
the new API adopts a midpoint extension for Lobatto and Radau in order to keep
the beam-axis contract uniform without introducing a pathological endpoint-only
rule into the baseline structural path. This is a computational convenience,
not a claim about classical one-point Lobatto/Radau theory, and it is
documented as such.

Architecturally, the key point is that the hot path remains static. The
quadrature family is selected at compile time, and
\texttt{TimoshenkoBeamN<N>} reconstructs its reduced shear interpolation from
the actual station coordinates exposed by the bound geometry rule. No runtime
dispatch is inserted in the quadrature loop.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Compile-time beam-axis quadrature selection used by the rebooted structural campaign.},label={lst:beam-axis-quadrature-selector}]
using GL3  = BeamAxisQuadratureT<BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLegendre, 3>;
using GLob = BeamAxisQuadratureT<BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLobatto, 3>;
using GRad = BeamAxisQuadratureT<BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussRadauLeft, 3>;

static_assert(BeamAxisQuadratureTraits<
    BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLegendre, 3>::polynomial_exactness_degree == 5);
static_assert(BeamAxisQuadratureTraits<
    BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLobatto, 3>::includes_left_endpoint);
\end{lstlisting}

This enabling layer is now frozen by
\texttt{tests/test\_beam\_axis\_quadrature.cpp}.  The regression constrains:
\begin{itemize}
  \item monomial exactness of the three rule families;
  \item mirror consistency of left/right Radau;
  \item reuse of the same \texttt{TimoshenkoBeamN} formulation with Lobatto
    and Radau section stations;
  \item and symmetry of the resulting structural tangent.
\end{itemize}
Methodologically, that is the correct precondition for the next structural
validation step: the column campaign may now compare integration families as an
explicit modeling choice rather than inheriting one silently from the element
implementation.

\section{Reduced RC column structural matrix}

The next layer of the reboot is no longer a generic workstream label but a
concrete computational matrix.  For the reduced reinforced-concrete column, the
current structural campaign is organized around the typed slice
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{S}_{N,q,\mathcal{K}}
  \;=\;
  \texttt{TimoshenkoBeamN<N>}
  \;+\;
  q
  \;+\;
  \mathcal{K},
\end{equation}
where \(N \in \{2,\dots,10\}\) is the beam interpolation order,
\(q \in \mathcal{Q}_{\text{beam}}\) is the beam-axis quadrature family, and
\(\mathcal{K}\) is the beam kinematic/formulation slice under audit.

The quadrature family set is now
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{Q}_{\text{beam}}
  =
  \left\{
    \text{Gauss--Legendre},
    \text{Gauss--Lobatto},
    \text{Gauss--Radau}_{L},
    \text{Gauss--Radau}_{R}
  \right\},
\end{equation}
while the formulation axis retained in the matrix is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{K}
  \in
  \left\{
    \text{small strain},
    \text{corotational},
    \text{Total Lagrangian},
    \text{Updated Lagrangian}
  \right\}.
\end{equation}
The crucial point is that this axis is kept \emph{even when the runtime path
does not exist}.  Otherwise the validation program would silently collapse the
set of desirable claims to the subset that happens to be implemented today.

This structural matrix now lives canonically in
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnStructuralMatrixCatalog.hh}.  Its present
reading is intentionally conservative and can be summarized as follows:
\begin{equation}
  \mathfrak{B}_{\text{phase3}}
  =
  \left\{
    \mathcal{S}_{N,q,\text{small strain}}
    \;:\;
    N=2,\dots,10,\;
    q \in \mathcal{Q}_{\text{beam}}
  \right\},
\end{equation}
that is, \(36\) runtime-ready baseline cases.
The two remaining subsets are not hidden:
\begin{align}
  \mathfrak{E}_{\text{CR}}
  &=
  \left\{
    \mathcal{S}_{N,q,\text{corotational}}
  \right\},
  &
  |\mathfrak{E}_{\text{CR}}| &= 36,
  \\
  \mathfrak{U}_{\text{finite}}
  &=
  \left\{
    \mathcal{S}_{N,q,\text{TL}},
    \mathcal{S}_{N,q,\text{UL}}
  \right\},
  &
  |\mathfrak{U}_{\text{finite}}| &= 72.
\end{align}
Here \(\mathfrak{E}_{\text{CR}}\) denotes a genuine \emph{family extension}
frontier: beam corotational kinematics exist elsewhere in the library, but not
yet as a \texttt{TimoshenkoBeamN<N>} family path.  By contrast,
\(\mathfrak{U}_{\text{finite}}\) denotes a \emph{missing formulation family}:
neither TL nor UL is currently a runtime beam formulation for this family, so
claiming them would require more than a local patch.

\begin{table}[htbp]
  \centering
  \caption{Current structural-matrix interpretation for the reduced RC column.}
  \label{tab:reduced-rc-column-structural-matrix}
  \small
  \begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.21\textwidth}p{0.15\textwidth}p{0.14\textwidth}p{0.15\textwidth}p{0.23\textwidth}@{}}
    \toprule
    \textbf{Slice family} & \textbf{Case count} & \textbf{Runtime path} &
    \textbf{Phase-3 baseline} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
    \midrule
    \(\mathcal{S}_{N,q,\text{small strain}}\)
    & 36 & yes & yes
    & Current audited reduced-column baseline. \\

    \(\mathcal{S}_{N,q,\text{corotational}}\)
    & 36 & no & no
    & Planned \texttt{TimoshenkoBeamN} kinematic extension; not yet a runtime
      path. \\

    \(\mathcal{S}_{N,q,\text{TL}}\),
    \(\mathcal{S}_{N,q,\text{UL}}\)
    & 72 & no & no
    & Not available for the present beam family; requires a distinct
      finite-kinematics beam formulation path. \\
    \bottomrule
  \end{tabular}
\end{table}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[
      node distance=8mm and 12mm,
      box/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=blue!5,
                  minimum width=34mm, minimum height=9mm},
      ext/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=orange!10,
                  minimum width=34mm, minimum height=9mm},
      miss/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=red!8,
                   minimum width=34mm, minimum height=9mm},
      arr/.style={-{Latex[length=2.5mm]}, thick}
    ]
    \node[box] (catalog) {ReducedRCColumn\\StructuralMatrixCatalog};
    \node[box, right=of catalog] (baseline) {ReducedRCColumn\\StructuralBaseline};
    \node[box, right=of baseline] (legacy) {Legacy wrapper\\TableCyclicValidationStructural};

    \node[ext, below=of baseline] (cr) {Corotational\\family extension};
    \node[miss, below=of cr] (finite) {TL / UL beam\\family absent};

    \draw[arr] (catalog) -- (baseline);
    \draw[arr] (baseline) -- (legacy);
    \draw[arr] (catalog) -- (cr);
    \draw[arr] (catalog) -- (finite);
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{The new reduced-column layer separates the current runtime baseline
  from two different kinds of missing scope: a planned corotational extension
  and a genuinely absent finite-kinematics beam family.}
  \label{fig:reduced-rc-column-structural-matrix}
\end{figure}

This split is not merely descriptive.  The runtime baseline is now also
available through
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnStructuralBaseline.hh/.cpp}, so the
legacy beam-column case no longer owns the only implementation of the reduced
column path.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={The reduced-column structural baseline now returns both global hysteresis and section-level observables through a clean runtime API.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-structural-baseline-api}]
using namespace fall_n::validation_reboot;

auto result = run_reduced_rc_column_small_strain_beam_case_result(
    ReducedRCColumnStructuralRunSpec{
        .beam_nodes = 3,
        .beam_axis_quadrature_family = BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLobatto,
        .axial_compression_force_mn = 0.02,
        .write_hysteresis_csv = false,
        .write_section_response_csv = false,
        .print_progress = false,
    },
    out_dir,
    cfg);

auto& hysteresis = result.hysteresis_records;
auto& base_side_section_history = result.section_response_records;
\end{lstlisting}

The corresponding regression,
\texttt{tests/test\_reduced\_rc\_column\_structural\_matrix.cpp}, freezes both
the compile-time counts and a small runtime smoke pass over the new baseline.
That smoke pass is intentionally modest: it does \emph{not} claim physical
validation yet.  It only proves that the new structural baseline can traverse
the same reduced-column path under the three audited quadrature families
without relying on the legacy monolithic driver.

\section{Reduced RC column claim--artifact--evidence matrix}

Once the structural matrix exists, one more distinction becomes necessary.
Knowing that a runtime slice is available does not yet answer what we are
scientifically allowed to claim about that slice.  For the reduced RC column,
the reboot therefore introduces an additional claim layer in
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnValidationClaimCatalog.hh}.

Formally, the phase-3 reduced-column claim set can be written as
\begin{equation}
  \mathfrak{C}_{\text{RC},\,\mathrm{phase3}}
  =
  \left\{
    C_q,\,
    C_{\mathrm{rt}},\,
    C_{N},\,
    C_{\sigma_N},\,
    C_{\mathrm{hys}},\,
    C_{M\kappa},\,
    C_{\mathrm{qsens}}
  \right\},
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{align}
  C_q &:\text{ the beam-axis quadrature family is an explicit modelling axis,}
  \\
  C_{\mathrm{rt}} &:\text{ the runtime beam-column surface exists for } N=2,\dots,10,
  \\
  C_N &:\text{ a node-refinement convergence claim can eventually be posed,}
  \\
  C_{\sigma_N} &:\text{ an optional axial-compression path exists,}
  \\
  C_{\mathrm{hys}} &:\text{ a base-shear-vs-drift hysteresis observable exists,}
  \\
  C_{M\kappa} &:\text{ a base-side moment-curvature observable exists at the active}
                 \text{ section station closest to the fixed end,}
  \\
  C_{\mathrm{qsens}} &:\text{ a quadrature-sensitivity claim can eventually be posed.}
\end{align}
The methodological point is that these claims are \emph{not} all at the same
readiness level.

For the reduced beam-column baseline, the moment-curvature observable is now
defined explicitly as
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{O}_{M\kappa}^{\mathrm{base}}
  :=
  \left\{
    \bigl(\kappa_y^{(g_\star)}(t_n),\,M_y^{(g_\star)}(t_n)\bigr)
  \right\}_{n=0}^{N_t},
  \qquad
  g_\star = \arg\min_g \xi_g,
\end{equation}
where \(\xi_g\) denotes the beam-axis coordinate of section station \(g\).
This definition is deliberate: for Lobatto and left-Radau rules,
\(g_\star\) may coincide with the boundary section, whereas for
Gauss--Legendre and right-Radau it is the nearest active station on the fixed
side.  The observable therefore exists cleanly at runtime, but its physical
interpretation still remains coupled to the quadrature-sensitivity benchmark.

\begin{table}[htbp]
  \centering
  \caption{Claim--artifact--evidence matrix for the reduced RC column baseline
  before physical benchmarking.}
  \label{tab:reduced-rc-column-claim-trace}
  \scriptsize
  \setlength{\tabcolsep}{3pt}
  \begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{@{}p{0.22\textwidth}p{0.18\textwidth}p{0.18\textwidth}p{0.12\textwidth}X@{}}
    \toprule
    \textbf{Claim} & \textbf{Artifact} & \textbf{Current evidence} &
    \textbf{Readiness} & \textbf{Next gate} \\
    \midrule
    Explicit beam-axis quadrature family
    & \texttt{BeamAxisQuadrature.hh}
    & exactness and station-symmetry regression
    & frozen enabler
    & none; this is an enabling contract, not a physical benchmark \\[0.4mm]

    Runtime reduced-column surface for \(N=2,\dots,10\)
    & \texttt{ReducedRCColumnStructuralBaseline}
    & matrix counts + runtime smoke
    & runtime-ready
    & node-refinement benchmark suite \\[0.4mm]

    Optional axial-compression path
    & \texttt{ReducedRCColumnStructuralBaseline}
    & finite axial-preload smoke run
    & runtime-ready
    & axial-load sensitivity suite \\[0.4mm]

    Hysteresis observable
    & \texttt{hysteresis.csv} writer contract
    & output-contract regression
    & runtime-ready
    & hysteresis-shape / dissipation benchmark suite \\[0.4mm]

    Base-side moment-curvature observable
    & \texttt{ReducedRCColumnStructuralBaseline} +
      \texttt{moment\_curvature\_base.csv}
    & output-contract regression for the active base-side section station
    & runtime-ready
    & section benchmark suite + quadrature-sensitivity interpretation \\[0.4mm]

    Node-refinement convergence
    & same runtime baseline
    & family exists, but no convergence benchmark
    & benchmark pending
    & close \(N=2 \rightarrow 10\) convergence table \\[0.4mm]

    Quadrature-family sensitivity
    & same runtime baseline + quadrature family
    & family exists, but no sensitivity benchmark
    & benchmark pending
    & close Gauss/Lobatto/Radau comparison suite \\
    \bottomrule
  \end{tabularx}
\end{table}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[
      node distance=8mm and 11mm,
      box/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=blue!5,
                  minimum width=33mm, minimum height=9mm},
      ready/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=green!8,
                    minimum width=33mm, minimum height=9mm},
      pend/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=orange!10,
                   minimum width=33mm, minimum height=9mm},
      miss/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=red!8,
                   minimum width=33mm, minimum height=9mm},
      arr/.style={-{Latex[length=2.5mm]}, thick}
    ]
    \node[box] (matrix) {Structural matrix\\\(\mathfrak{B}_{\mathrm{phase3}}\)};
    \node[ready, right=of matrix] (runtime) {Runtime-ready claims\\\(C_{\mathrm{rt}}, C_{\sigma_N}, C_{\mathrm{hys}}, C_{M\kappa}\)};
    \node[pend, below=of runtime] (bench) {Benchmark-pending claims\\\(C_N, C_{\mathrm{qsens}}\)};
    \node[pend, below=of matrix] (inst) {Prebenchmark caveat\\base-side station \(\neq\) exact boundary in general};
    \node[box, above=of runtime] (enabler) {Frozen enabler\\\(C_q\)};

    \draw[arr] (matrix) -- (runtime);
    \draw[arr] (matrix) -- (inst);
    \draw[arr] (runtime) -- (bench);
    \draw[arr] (enabler) -- (runtime);
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{The reduced RC column reboot now distinguishes between
  runtime-ready claims and benchmark-pending claims while making explicit that
  the moment-curvature observable now lives at the active base-side station,
  not necessarily at the exact boundary section.  This prevents the structural
  campaign from inheriting physical validation status from a mere smoke run.}
  \label{fig:reduced-rc-column-claim-trace}
\end{figure}

The practical reading of Table~\ref{tab:reduced-rc-column-claim-trace} is
strict.  No row is currently allowed to anchor a physical benchmark by itself.
The catalog deliberately separates three states that are often blurred in
validation work:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the numerical surface exists and runs;
  \item the corresponding observable exists and is exported cleanly;
  \item the scientific claim supported by that observable has been benchmarked
    against theory, refinement, or experiment.
\end{enumerate}
At the present stage of the reboot, the reduced RC column has reached
State~1 for the full small-strain beam family and State~2 for both the global
hysteresis and the base-side moment-curvature observables.  What remains open
is State~3: benchmark closure.  In particular, the moment-curvature observable
must still be interpreted against the quadrature family because the controlling
station is the nearest active fixed-side section, not a quadrature-independent
ideal boundary cut.  The reboot now also has an independent section-level
baseline, solved by enforcing
\(
  N(\varepsilon_0,\kappa_y)=N^\star
\)
at each curvature step over the same fiber-section ingredients.  This improves
the evidence hierarchy substantially.  The reboot now also has an explicit
comparison artifact between both objects, implemented in
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnMomentCurvatureClosure.hh/.cpp}.  The
comparison is carried out over the physically relevant control variable,
curvature, not over the raw step counter, and it uses the sign of the active
structural branch to map the first monotonic loading path to the canonical
positive section branch.  For the current representative slice
\((N=4,\;\text{Gauss--Lobatto})\), the closure bundle already shows tight
flexural agreement, with
\[
  \eta_M
  =
  \frac{|M_{\mathrm{str}}-M_{\mathrm{sec}}|}
       {\max(|M_{\mathrm{sec}}|,\varepsilon)}
  \lesssim 2.3\times 10^{-3},
  \qquad
  \eta_{K_t}
  =
  \frac{|K_{t,\mathrm{str}}-K_{t,\mathrm{sec}}|}
       {\max(|K_{t,\mathrm{sec}}|,\varepsilon)}
  \lesssim 1.8\times 10^{-3},
\]
and secant-stiffness mismatch of the same order.  The reboot now also has the
corresponding matrix-level artifact in
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnMomentCurvatureClosureMatrix.hh/.cpp},
which sweeps the full runtime-ready family
\(
  \mathfrak{B}_{\text{phase3}}
\)
over \(N=2,\dots,10\) and the four explicit beam-axis quadrature families.
For the current monotonic audit protocol, the matrix result is strong: all
\(36\) runtime-ready slices complete, all \(36\) satisfy the representative
closure tolerances including axial force, the worst moment/secant mismatch is
about \(5.095\times 10^{-7}\) (at the
\texttt{n05\_gauss\_radau\_left\_small\_strain} slice), the worst tangent
mismatch is about \(2.178\times 10^{-9}\) (at
\texttt{n08\_gauss\_legendre\_small\_strain}), and the worst axial-force
mismatch is about \(2.677\times 10^{-7}\) (also at
\texttt{n08\_gauss\_legendre\_small\_strain}).  The node-wise spread remains
mild and now sits in the sub-micro range, while the quadrature-family
averages remain clustered within the narrow band
\(
  3.378\times 10^{-7}
  \lesssim
  \overline{\eta_M}^{(q)}
  \lesssim
  4.518\times 10^{-7}
\).

That previous limitation has now been removed.  The structural baseline no
longer injects the axial compression only as a nodal load superposed on the
lateral branch.  Instead, it executes an explicit equilibrated axial-preload
stage and then holds the converged preload during the lateral displacement
history.  Re-running the full \(36\)-case matrix under that staged protocol
collapses the axial diagnostic from order unity to
\(2.677\times 10^{-7}\), while the worst moment/secant mismatch drops to
\(5.095\times 10^{-7}\) and the worst tangent mismatch to
\(2.178\times 10^{-9}\).  In other words, the internal structural-versus-
section closure gate is now closed simultaneously in axial force, moment,
secant stiffness and tangent stiffness over the full runtime-ready matrix.

The campaign nevertheless remains \emph{pre-benchmark} in the strict sense of
this reboot.  The open issue has moved: it is no longer preload consistency,
but benchmark closure against refinement trends, quadrature sensitivity and
external column-level reference data.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Independent section-level baseline now available for the reduced RC column reboot.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-section-baseline}]
using namespace fall_n::validation_reboot;

const auto result =
    run_reduced_rc_column_section_moment_curvature_baseline(
        ReducedRCColumnSectionBaselineRunSpec{
            .target_axial_compression_force_mn = 0.02,
            .max_curvature_y = 0.03,
            .steps = 120,
        },
        "data/output/cyclic_validation/reduced_column_section_baseline");
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Representative structural-versus-section closure bundle for the reduced RC column reboot.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-moment-curvature-closure}]

\paragraph{Internal node-refinement matrix.}
The next internal obligation is no longer the structural-versus-section
consistency gate, which is already closed, but the stabilization of the
reduced family as the number of beam nodes/sections increases.  A first
runtime artifact for that purpose is now kept in
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnNodeRefinementStudy.hh/.cpp}.  The
study is intentionally internal: for each beam-axis quadrature family \(q\),
it uses the highest runtime-ready slice \(N_{\mathrm{ref}}=10\) as an
intrinsic reference and compares every lower-\(N\) branch against that slice
on the common curvature interval.  The main drift measures are
\begin{equation}
  \eta_{M}^{(N,q)}
  =
  \max_{\kappa \in [0,\kappa_{\max}^{(N,q,\cap)}]}
  \frac{|M_{N,q}(\kappa)-M_{N_{\mathrm{ref}},q}(\kappa)|}
       {\max(|M_{N_{\mathrm{ref}},q}(\kappa)|,\varepsilon)},
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
  \eta_{M,\mathrm{term}}^{(N,q)}
  =
  \frac{|M_{N,q}(\kappa_{\max}^{(N,q,\cap)})-
         M_{N_{\mathrm{ref}},q}(\kappa_{\max}^{(N,q,\cap)})|}
       {\max(|M_{N_{\mathrm{ref}},q}(\kappa_{\max}^{(N,q,\cap)})|,\varepsilon)},
\end{equation}
with analogous definitions for tangent and secant stiffness.  Here
\(\kappa_{\max}^{(N,q,\cap)}\) is the largest curvature shared by the pair of
branches.  This definition matters: it avoids confusing a true refinement
effect with a mere mismatch in the terminal sampling point.

On the current full monotonic runtime-ready matrix
\(\{N=2,\dots,10\}\times\{\text{Gauss},\text{Lobatto},\text{Radau-left},\text{Radau-right}\}\),
all \(36/36\) cases complete and all \(36/36\) satisfy the representative
internal-refinement gate.  The worst terminal-moment drift is about
\(1.41\times 10^{-4}\), the worst pointwise moment drift about
\(2.14\times 10^{-4}\), the worst tangent drift about
\(5.03\times 10^{-7}\), and the worst secant drift about
\(5.04\times 10^{-5}\).  The drift decays strongly as \(N\) increases and is
exactly zero at \(N=10\) by construction, because that slice is the family
reference.  This closes the monotonic full-matrix part of the refinement
question. What remained open after that result was not the monotonic matrix
itself, but whether the same base-side observable would remain stable once
unloading and reloading were introduced.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Internal monotonic node-refinement matrix for the reduced RC column reboot.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-node-refinement-study}]
using namespace fall_n::validation_reboot;
using fall_n::table_cyclic_validation::CyclicValidationRunConfig;

const auto refinement =
    run_reduced_rc_column_node_refinement_study(
        ReducedRCColumnNodeRefinementRunSpec{
            .closure_spec = {
                .structural_spec = {
                    .axial_compression_force_mn = 0.02,
                    .use_equilibrated_axial_preload_stage = true,
                    .axial_preload_steps = 4,
                },
                .section_spec = {
                    .steps = 12,
                },
                .structural_protocol = CyclicValidationRunConfig{
                    .protocol_name = "reduced_node_refinement",
                    .execution_profile_name = "default",
                    .amplitudes_m = {2.5e-3},
                    .steps_per_segment = 4,
                    .max_bisections = 4,
                },
            },
        },
        "data/output/cyclic_validation/reduced_column_node_refinement");
\end{lstlisting}

  The artifact does not yet claim external validation; it now quantifies over
  the full monotonic runtime-ready matrix how the reduced family stabilizes
  against its highest internal reference before any column-level benchmark is
  called closed.}
\label{fig:reduced-rc-column-node-refinement-study}
\end{figure}

\paragraph{Representative cyclic node-refinement pilot.}
That next question is no longer open only in words. A second artifact,
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnCyclicNodeRefinementStudy.hh/.cpp},
now executes a first representative cyclic refinement pilot over
\(\{N=2,4,10\}\times\{\text{Gauss--Legendre},\text{Gauss--Lobatto}\}\)
with two amplitudes \(\{1.25,2.50\}\,\mathrm{mm}\), axial preload
\(0.02\,\mathrm{MN}\), and the same base-side section observable used by the
monotonic study. The pilot reuses the highest-\(N\) case inside each
quadrature family as the cyclic internal reference and reports:
\begin{equation}
  \eta_{M,\mathrm{return}}^{(N,q)}
  =
  \frac{|M_{N,q}^{\mathrm{return}}-
         M_{N_{\mathrm{ref}},q}^{\mathrm{return}}|}
       {\max(|M_{N_{\mathrm{ref}},q}^{\mathrm{return}}|,\varepsilon)},
\end{equation}
the full-history drift
\begin{equation}
  \eta_{M,\mathrm{hist}}^{(N,q)}
  =
  \max_{\tau \in \mathcal{T}_{\cap}}
  \frac{|M_{N,q}(\tau)-M_{N_{\mathrm{ref}},q}(\tau)|}
       {\max(|M_{N_{\mathrm{ref}},q}(\tau)|,\varepsilon)},
\end{equation}
the turning-point drift, the tangent-history drift, the axial-force-history
drift, and the shift of the controlling base-side station. Here
\(\mathcal{T}_{\cap}\) denotes the common pseudo-time support after aligning
the cyclic histories case-by-case inside each family.

The current pilot is already informative. All \(6/6\) cases complete, but
only \(3/6\) satisfy the representative cyclic gate. The worst terminal return
moment drift is about \(2.80\times 10^{-1}\), the worst full-history moment
drift and worst turning-point drift are both about \(6.33\times 10^{-1}\),
the worst tangent-history drift is about \(4.53\times 10^{-3}\), the worst
axial-force-history drift only about \(1.74\times 10^{-5}\), and the worst
base-side station shift is \(1.0\) in parent coordinates. This is a useful
scientific separation: the current cyclic frontier is dominated by
reversal-sensitive moment history and station migration, not by axial-force
mismatch and not by tangent collapse.

Methodologically, the pilot also forced one correction. The secant-history
drift is still written to the CSV bundle, but it is no longer used as the
representative cyclic acceptance gate. Near unloading and reloading
crossings, the secant denominator becomes ill-conditioned as curvature passes
near zero, so a full-history secant norm can report very large values even
when the underlying cyclic response remains interpretable. The cyclic gate is
therefore now based on return moment, history moment, turning-point,
tangent-history, and axial-force-history drift, while secant drift remains an
explicit diagnostic channel.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Representative cyclic node-refinement pilot for the reduced RC column reboot.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-cyclic-node-refinement-study}]
using namespace fall_n::validation_reboot;
using fall_n::table_cyclic_validation::CyclicValidationRunConfig;

const auto cyclic_refinement =
    run_reduced_rc_column_cyclic_node_refinement_study(
        ReducedRCColumnCyclicNodeRefinementRunSpec{
            .structural_spec = {
                .axial_compression_force_mn = 0.02,
                .use_equilibrated_axial_preload_stage = true,
                .axial_preload_steps = 4,
                .write_section_response_csv = true,
            },
            .structural_protocol = CyclicValidationRunConfig{
                .protocol_name = "reduced_node_refinement_cyclic_pilot",
                .execution_profile_name = "default",
                .amplitudes_m = {1.25e-3, 2.50e-3},
                .steps_per_segment = 2,
                .max_bisections = 4,
            },
            .beam_nodes_filter = {2, 4, 10},
            .quadrature_family_filter = {
                BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLegendre,
                BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLobatto,
            },
        },
        "data/output/cyclic_validation/reboot_cyclic_node_refinement_study_pilot");
\end{lstlisting}

  column reboot. The pilot established the first honest separation of the
  cyclic frontier: reversal-sensitive moment-history drift and station
  migration dominate long before axial-force drift becomes critical.}
  \label{fig:reduced-rc-column-cyclic-node-refinement-study}
\end{figure}

\paragraph{Full cyclic node-refinement matrix.}
The representative pilot is no longer the end of the story. The same
\texttt{ReducedRCColumnCyclicNodeRefinementStudy} artifact now executes the
entire runtime-ready cyclic matrix
\(\{N=2,\dots,10\}\times\{\text{Gauss--Legendre},\text{Gauss--Lobatto},\text{Gauss--Radau-left},\text{Gauss--Radau-right}\}\)
under the same displacement-driven protocol semantics. On that full matrix,
all \(36/36\) cases complete, but only \(8/36\) satisfy the representative
cyclic internal gate. The worst terminal return-moment drift is about
\(8.40\times 10^{-1}\), the worst full-history moment drift and the worst
turning-point drift are both about \(8.40\times 10^{-1}\), the worst
tangent-history drift remains only about \(4.53\times 10^{-3}\), the worst
axial-force-history drift about \(1.74\times 10^{-5}\), and the largest
base-side station shift remains \(1.0\) in parent coordinates. This matters:
the open structural frontier is now narrower and more specific than ``the
cyclic matrix is missing''. The cyclic matrix exists; what remains open is
closure of the declared observable under reversal-sensitive history transport
and station migration.

\paragraph{Implementation note on postprocessing compactness.}
The cyclic node-refinement artifact now follows the same compactness rule
already adopted for the continuation and cyclic quadrature bundles: repeated
min/max/average reductions are expressed through small local accumulators,
turning-point detection lives behind a dedicated helper, and tolerance
projection is written through short local lambdas. This does not modify the
numerical benchmark contract, but it reduces bookkeeping verbosity in the
validation layer and therefore lowers the risk of maintenance drift between
case-level, node-level, and global summary tables.

\paragraph{Continuation sensitivity near reversal.}
That narrower frontier immediately raises the next numerical question: how
much of the residual cyclic drift belongs to the constitutive--discrete model,
and how much is an artifact of the continuation schedule itself when the
loading direction changes. A third artifact,
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnCyclicContinuationSensitivityStudy.hh/.cpp},
therefore compares two declared policies on the same full matrix:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item monolithic incremental displacement control;
  \item reversal-guarded incremental displacement control, which refines the
        same displacement-driven target protocol near sign changes without
        silently changing the benchmark semantics.
\end{enumerate}
The guarded policy keeps \(36/36\) completed cases and the same
\(8/36\) representative passes. It therefore does \emph{not} close the
frontier by itself. It does, however, improve terminal return drift in
\(16/36\) cases, full-history moment drift in \(19/36\), turning-point drift
in \(19/36\), secant drift in \(15/36\), and axial-force drift in \(32/36\),
while leaving the controlling-station shift unchanged in every case. The
scientific reading is precise: guarded displacement control is worthwhile and
should remain part of the declared benchmark policy space, but the current
cyclic frontier cannot honestly be reduced to a mere continuation failure.
Only after this displacement-driven sensitivity bundle is exhausted does it
become legitimate to ask whether a stronger continuation such as arc-length
should be introduced as a \emph{new} benchmark policy, rather than smuggled
into the current one \cite{Crisfield1991_NLFEA_Vol1}.

\paragraph{Implementation note on compactness and traceability.}
This continuation-sensitivity artifact now follows the same compaction
criterion adopted in the newer quadrature and readiness studies: repeated
baseline/candidate/delta reductions are expressed through small local
accumulators and lambda-based observers, instead of long blocks of manual
field-by-field updates. This is not merely stylistic. The continuation bundle
produces case rows, node summaries, and global maxima over the same set of
observables; keeping those reductions factored in one place lowers the risk of
semantic drift between tables while leaving the numerical solve itself
untouched.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Continuation-sensitivity study for the full reduced cyclic node-refinement matrix.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-cyclic-continuation-sensitivity-study}]
using namespace fall_n::validation_reboot;
using fall_n::table_cyclic_validation::CyclicValidationRunConfig;

const CyclicValidationRunConfig cyclic_protocol{
    .protocol_name = "reduced_node_refinement_cyclic_full",
    .execution_profile_name = "default",
    .amplitudes_m = {1.25e-3, 2.50e-3},
    .steps_per_segment = 2,
    .max_bisections = 4,
};

const auto continuation_sensitivity =
    run_reduced_rc_column_cyclic_continuation_sensitivity_study(
        ReducedRCColumnCyclicContinuationSensitivityRunSpec{
            .baseline_spec = {
                .structural_spec = {
                    .axial_compression_force_mn = 0.02,
                    .use_equilibrated_axial_preload_stage = true,
                    .axial_preload_steps = 4,
                },
                .structural_protocol = cyclic_protocol,
            },
            .candidate_spec = {
                .structural_spec = {
                    .axial_compression_force_mn = 0.02,
                    .use_equilibrated_axial_preload_stage = true,
                    .axial_preload_steps = 4,
                    .continuation_kind =
                        ReducedRCColumnContinuationKind::
                            reversal_guarded_incremental_displacement_control,
                    .continuation_segment_substep_factor = 2,
                },
                .structural_protocol = cyclic_protocol,
            },
        },
        "data/output/cyclic_validation/"
        "reboot_cyclic_continuation_sensitivity_study_full");
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[
      node distance=8mm and 10mm,
      box/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=blue!5,
                  minimum width=34mm, minimum height=9mm},
      proc/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=green!8,
                   minimum width=40mm, minimum height=9mm},
      eval/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=orange!10,
                   minimum width=42mm, minimum height=9mm},
      resultbox/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=red!8,
                        minimum width=43mm, minimum height=9mm},
      arr/.style={-{Latex[length=2.5mm]}, thick}
    ]
    \node[box] (baseline) {Baseline policy\\Monolithic displacement control};
    \node[box, right=of baseline] (guarded) {Candidate policy\\Reversal-guarded displacement control};
    \node[proc, below=of baseline] (run) {Run the same cyclic matrix\\under both declared policies};
    \node[eval, right=of run] (compare) {Compare \(\eta_{M,\mathrm{return}}\), \(\eta_{M,\mathrm{hist}}\),\\\(\eta_{K_t}\), \(\eta_{K_s}\), \(\eta_N\), \(\Delta\xi_{\mathrm{base}}\)};
    \node[resultbox, below=of compare] (decision) {Freeze displacement-control policy\\or justify explicit escalation to arc-length};

    \draw[arr] (baseline) -- (run);
    \draw[arr] (guarded) -- (compare);
    \draw[arr] (run) -- (compare);
    \draw[arr] (compare) -- (decision);
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{Continuation-policy sensitivity around cyclic reversals. Arc-length
  is not treated as an invisible numerical patch; it becomes admissible only
  after the displacement-driven sensitivity bundle has been exhausted and the
  escalation is justified explicitly.}
  \label{fig:reduced-rc-column-cyclic-continuation-sensitivity}
\end{figure}

\paragraph{Internal quadrature-sensitivity matrix.}
The other internal ambiguity that had to be pulled out of the shadows is not
refinement, but \emph{section-station placement}. For the reduced beam family,
changing the beam-axis quadrature rule changes both the numerical integration
and the location of the active base-side section station from which the
moment-curvature observable is extracted. The quadrature-sensitivity study now
kept in
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnQuadratureSensitivityStudy.hh/.cpp}
therefore measures each family \(f\) against a declared reference family
\(f_{\mathrm{ref}}=\) Gauss--Legendre at the same beam-node count \(N\). The
main spread measures are
\begin{equation}
  \eta_{M}^{(N,f\mid f_{\mathrm{ref}})}
  =
  \max_{\kappa \in [0,\kappa_{\max}^{(N,f,\cap)}]}
  \frac{|M_{N,f}(\kappa)-M_{N,f_{\mathrm{ref}}}(\kappa)|}
       {\max(|M_{N,f_{\mathrm{ref}}}(\kappa)|,\varepsilon)},
\end{equation}
and the explicit station-shift observable
\begin{equation}
  \Delta \xi_{\mathrm{base}}^{(N,f\mid f_{\mathrm{ref}})}
  =
  \left|
    \xi_{\mathrm{base}}^{(N,f)} -
    \xi_{\mathrm{base}}^{(N,f_{\mathrm{ref}})}
  \right|.
\end{equation}
This distinction matters scientifically: a family-to-family response spread is
not interpreted honestly unless the displacement of the active base-side
station is also reported.

On the current full monotonic runtime-ready matrix
\(\{N=2,\dots,10\}\times\{\text{Gauss},\text{Lobatto},\text{Radau-left},\text{Radau-right}\}\),
all \(36/36\) cases complete and all \(36/36\) satisfy the representative
internal-sensitivity gate. The worst terminal-moment spread is about
\(1.17\times 10^{-4}\), the worst pointwise moment spread about
\(2.41\times 10^{-4}\), the worst tangent spread about
\(3.73\times 10^{-4}\), the worst secant spread about
\(1.74\times 10^{-4}\), and the largest controlling-station shift about
\(4.23\times 10^{-1}\) in parent coordinates. The \(N=2\) slices collapse to
zero spread by symmetry, and both response spread and station shift decay as
\(N\) grows. This closes the monotonic full-matrix part of the
quadrature-sensitivity question. What remains open is the cyclic
family-spread bundle and the interpretation of station movement under
unloading and reloading.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Internal quadrature-sensitivity matrix for the reduced RC column reboot.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-quadrature-sensitivity-study}]
using namespace fall_n::validation_reboot;
using fall_n::table_cyclic_validation::CyclicValidationRunConfig;

const auto spread =
    run_reduced_rc_column_quadrature_sensitivity_study(
        ReducedRCColumnQuadratureSensitivityRunSpec{
            .closure_spec = {
                .structural_spec = {
                    .axial_compression_force_mn = 0.02,
                    .use_equilibrated_axial_preload_stage = true,
                    .axial_preload_steps = 4,
                },
                .section_spec = {
                    .steps = 12,
                },
                .structural_protocol = CyclicValidationRunConfig{
                    .protocol_name = "reduced_quadrature_sensitivity",
                    .execution_profile_name = "default",
                    .amplitudes_m = {2.5e-3},
                    .steps_per_segment = 4,
                    .max_bisections = 4,
                },
            },
            .reference_family = BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLegendre,
        },
        "data/output/cyclic_validation/reduced_column_quadrature_sensitivity");
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[
      node distance=8mm and 10mm,
      box/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=blue!5,
                  minimum width=34mm, minimum height=9mm},
      ref/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=orange!10,
                  minimum width=40mm, minimum height=9mm},
      proc/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=green!8,
                   minimum width=38mm, minimum height=9mm},
      resultbox/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=red!8,
                        minimum width=40mm, minimum height=9mm},
      arr/.style={-{Latex[length=2.5mm]}, thick}
    ]
    \node[box] (cases) {Runtime-ready cases\\\((N,f)\)};
    \node[ref, right=of cases] (refcase) {Pick reference family\\\(f_{\mathrm{ref}}=\) Gauss--Legendre};
    \node[proc, right=of refcase] (interp) {Interpolate common branch\\and recover \(\xi_{\mathrm{base}}\)};
    \node[resultbox, below=of interp] (metrics) {Write spread tables\\\(\eta_M,\eta_{K_t},\eta_{K_s},\Delta\xi_{\mathrm{base}}\)};

    \draw[arr] (cases) -- (refcase);
    \draw[arr] (refcase) -- (interp);
    \draw[arr] (interp) -- (metrics);
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{Internal quadrature-sensitivity study used by the reduced RC
  column reboot. The artifact makes the family-to-family spread explicit and,
  crucially, reports the shift of the active base-side section station instead
  of hiding station-placement effects under a generic numerical-error label.}
  \label{fig:reduced-rc-column-quadrature-sensitivity-study}
\end{figure}

\paragraph{Full cyclic quadrature-family spread under declared continuation.}
The same family-spread question is no longer open only as an intention.  It
now executes over the full runtime-ready cyclic matrix under the declared
continuation policy
\texttt{reversal\_guarded\_incremental\_displacement\_control} with segment
substep factor \(2\), keeping Gauss--Legendre as the explicit reference family
at each \(N\).  On that full cyclic bundle, all \(36/36\) cases complete, but
only \(14/36\) satisfy the representative cyclic family-spread gate.  The
worst terminal return-moment spread, pointwise moment-history spread, and
turning-point spread all reach about \(9.42\times 10^{-1}\); the worst
tangent-history spread is about \(1.32\times 10^{-1}\), whereas the worst
axial-force-history spread remains only about \(9.25\times 10^{-7}\).  The
largest controlling-station shift remains about \(4.23\times 10^{-1}\) in
parent coordinates.  The secant spread can grow to about \(8.18\), which is
precisely why it remains a diagnostic-only channel near reversal crossings
instead of entering the representative cyclic gate.

This sharpens the interpretation considerably.  The unresolved cyclic
quadrature frontier is not a generic loss of equilibrium and not a failure of
the reference family to execute.  Gauss--Legendre passes \(9/9\) reference
cases; by contrast, Gauss--Lobatto passes \(2/9\), Radau-left \(1/9\), and
Radau-right \(2/9\).  The remaining open question is therefore narrower and
more honest: before escalating to a stronger continuation such as arc-length,
the campaign must first freeze the structural reference family and decide how
to interpret the reversal-sensitive family spread induced by alternative
section-station placements.

\paragraph{Implementation note on compaction and traceability.}
This study was also used as a cleanup point for the validation code itself.
The internal reductions that project case-level metrics into node, family, and
overall summaries are now expressed through small accumulator objects and local
\emph{lambda}-based group builders rather than repeated field-by-field update
blocks.  The intent is not stylistic minimalism; it is semantic stability.
When the same metric pattern is written once and reused, the risk of drifting
definitions between CSV tables is reduced.  Because these helpers live in the
postprocessing and audit layer, they improve maintainability without burdening
the numerical hot path.

The same compactness rule has now been extended to the monotonic
node-refinement and monotonic quadrature-sensitivity bundles as well.  Their
group summaries now follow the same accumulator-based projection and short
predicate-driven reference counting used by the cyclic artifacts.  This does
not change a single benchmark metric, but it removes another source of
bookkeeping asymmetry between the monotonic and cyclic evidence layers.

\paragraph{Implementation note on solver-trace hygiene.}
The reduced-column structural baseline now also drives the low-level
Newton/bisection trace through an explicit switch,
\texttt{NonlinearAnalysis::set\_incremental\_logging(bool)}.  When a study
declares \texttt{print\_progress = false}, the same slice is still solved, but
the harness no longer drowns in per-substep chatter from the nonlinear
incremental engine.  This is not a numerical change; it is a boundary cleanup.
The benchmark-level output is now closer to the actual object of validation:
case summaries, CSV evidence bundles and declared continuation outcomes.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Full cyclic quadrature-family spread study under the declared reduced-column continuation policy.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-cyclic-quadrature-sensitivity-study}]
using namespace fall_n::validation_reboot;
using fall_n::table_cyclic_validation::CyclicValidationRunConfig;

const auto cyclic_family_spread =
    run_reduced_rc_column_cyclic_quadrature_sensitivity_study(
        ReducedRCColumnCyclicQuadratureSensitivityRunSpec{
            .structural_spec = {
                .axial_compression_force_mn = 0.02,
                .use_equilibrated_axial_preload_stage = true,
                .axial_preload_steps = 4,
            },
            .structural_protocol = CyclicValidationRunConfig{
                .protocol_name = "reduced_cyclic_quadrature_sensitivity",
                .execution_profile_name = "default",
                .amplitudes_m = {1.25e-3, 2.50e-3},
                .steps_per_segment = 2,
                .max_bisections = 4,
            },
            .reference_family = BeamAxisQuadratureFamily::GaussLegendre,
            .continuation_kind =
                ReducedRCColumnContinuationKind::
                    reversal_guarded_incremental_displacement_control,
            .continuation_segment_substep_factor = 2,
        },
        "data/output/cyclic_validation/"
        "reboot_cyclic_quadrature_sensitivity_study_full");
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Canonical reduced-column claim matrix used by the reboot.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-claim-trace}]
constexpr auto claims =
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_validation_claim_table_v;

static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_claim_runtime_baseline_anchor_count_v == 5);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_claim_instrumentation_pending_count_v == 0);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_claim_physical_benchmark_anchor_count_v == 0);
\end{lstlisting}

\section{Reduced RC column claim-to-benchmark closure matrix}

The claim matrix above is still not the full validation object.  It freezes
what the code is allowed to claim and what evidence exists today, but it does
not yet freeze the \emph{benchmark obligation} that remains attached to each
open claim.  That extra bridge is now kept canonically in
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnBenchmarkTraceCatalog.hh}.

For the reduced structural column, the benchmark-trace object can be written
schematically as
\begin{equation}
  \mathfrak{T}_{\mathrm{RC},\,\mathrm{bench}}
  =
  \left\{
    \bigl(C_i,\;B_i,\;\mathcal{O}_i,\;\mathcal{R}_i,\;G_i\bigr)
  \right\}_{i=1}^{6},
\end{equation}
where \(C_i\) is an open reduced-column claim, \(B_i\) the benchmark family
that must be executed, \(\mathcal{O}_i\) the primary observable used for the
comparison, \(\mathcal{R}_i\) the corresponding reference class, and \(G_i\)
the acceptance gate that would close if the benchmark passed.  This follows
the same logic already fixed by the continuum and constitutive chapters:
claims are not validated by existence alone, but by comparing an observable
derived from an energetically consistent discrete object against a declared
reference class \cite{Crisfield1991_NLFEA_Vol1,DeBorst2012_NonlinearFEM}.

\begin{table}[htbp]
  \centering
  \caption{Claim-to-benchmark closure matrix for the reduced RC column reboot.}
  \label{tab:reduced-rc-column-benchmark-trace}
  \scriptsize
  \setlength{\tabcolsep}{3pt}
  \begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{@{}p{0.19\textwidth}p{0.19\textwidth}p{0.17\textwidth}p{0.17\textwidth}X@{}}
    \toprule
    \textbf{Open claim} & \textbf{Benchmark family} & \textbf{Primary observable}
    & \textbf{Reference class} & \textbf{Acceptance gate closed if passed} \\
    \midrule
    Runtime reduced-column surface
    & runtime-surface matrix
    & base shear vs drift envelope across \(N\) and quadrature families
    & internal runtime-matrix consistency
    & every audited small-strain baseline slice completes with finite response
      and auditable output contracts; this closes the claim itself but is not
      yet a physical benchmark gate. \\[0.4mm]

    Optional axial-compression path
    & axial-load interaction suite
    & base shear vs drift under constant axial preload
    & audited experimental or literature datasets with reported axial-load level
    & axial-load sensitivity becomes eligible to act as part of the phase-3
      structural physical benchmark. \\[0.4mm]

    Hysteresis observable
    & cyclic hysteresis protocol suite
    & base shear vs drift loops
    & audited experimental or literature hysteresis envelopes
    & loop shape, strength degradation, and cycle dissipation become eligible
      to anchor the phase-3 structural physical benchmark. \\[0.4mm]

    Base-side moment-curvature observable
    & base-side section benchmark suite
    & \(\mathcal{O}_{M\kappa}^{\mathrm{base}}\)
    & independent section-level moment-curvature baseline
    & the section observable ceases to be only a runtime contract and becomes
      an audited structural benchmark channel. \\[0.4mm]

    Node-refinement convergence
    & node-refinement suite
    & base-side moment-curvature and terminal-moment drift versus \(N\)
    & internal runtime matrix interpreted as a convergence study
    & refinement no longer remains an unquantified aspiration; it becomes a
      closed precondition for the phase-3 structural benchmark. \\[0.4mm]

    Quadrature-family sensitivity
    & quadrature-sensitivity suite
    & base-side moment-curvature spread across Gauss/Lobatto/Radau families
    & internal runtime matrix interpreted as a controlled section-placement study
    & quadrature dependence is bounded and made explicit instead of being
      hidden as numerical noise. \\
    \bottomrule
  \end{tabularx}
\end{table}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[
      node distance=8mm and 10mm,
      box/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=blue!5,
                  minimum width=33mm, minimum height=9mm},
      bench/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=green!8,
                    minimum width=34mm, minimum height=9mm},
      ref/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=orange!10,
                  minimum width=35mm, minimum height=9mm},
      gate/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=red!8,
                   minimum width=36mm, minimum height=9mm},
      arr/.style={-{Latex[length=2.5mm]}, thick}
    ]
    \node[box] (claim) {Open claim\\\(C_i\)};
    \node[bench, right=of claim] (bench) {Benchmark family\\\(B_i\)};
    \node[ref, right=of bench] (ref) {Reference class\\\(\mathcal{R}_i\)};
    \node[gate, below=of bench] (gate) {Acceptance gate\\\(G_i\)};

    \draw[arr] (claim) -- (bench);
    \draw[arr] (bench) -- (ref);
    \draw[arr] (bench) -- (gate);
    \draw[arr] (ref.south) |- (gate.east);
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{The reduced-column reboot is now traceable one step further:
  every open claim is attached to a concrete benchmark family, a declared
  reference class, and an explicit gate.  This prevents the campaign from
  turning smoke runs or CSV contracts into de facto validation evidence.}
  \label{fig:reduced-rc-column-benchmark-trace}
\end{figure}

Two consequences of Table~\ref{tab:reduced-rc-column-benchmark-trace} are worth
stating explicitly.
\begin{enumerate}
  \item The runtime-surface benchmark is \emph{not} itself a physical benchmark
    gate.  Its role is to prove that the auditable baseline family really
    exists over the declared \(N \times q\) matrix.
  \item The base-side moment-curvature benchmark is intentionally tied first to
    an independent section baseline rather than directly to a full structural
    experiment.  This is scientifically stricter: it isolates the beam-column
    reduction error from the later physical discrepancy between model and test.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Canonical reduced-column benchmark trace used by the reboot.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-benchmark-trace}]
constexpr auto trace =
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_benchmark_trace_table_v;

static_assert(trace.size() == 6);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_benchmark_external_reference_count_v == 2);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_benchmark_section_baseline_count_v == 1);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_phase3_structural_benchmark_gate_count_v == 5);
\end{lstlisting}

\section{Reduced RC column evidence-closure matrix}

The benchmark-trace layer still answers only \emph{which} benchmark family must
be executed.  A final layer is required before the campaign can be run as a
scientific program instead of a roadmap:
\begin{quote}
  \emph{What evidence artifact already exists, what concrete numerical
  experiment is still missing, and what closure artifact would transform the
  open claim into benchmark evidence?}
\end{quote}
This additional bridge is now frozen canonically in
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCColumnEvidenceClosureCatalog.hh}.

For the reduced RC column, the evidence-closure object is represented as
\begin{equation}
  \mathfrak{E}_{\mathrm{RC}}
  =
  \left\{
    \bigl(C_i,\;B_i,\;A_i^{\mathrm{now}},\;X_i^{\mathrm{miss}},\;A_i^{\mathrm{close}}\bigr)
  \right\}_{i=1}^{6},
\end{equation}
where \(C_i\) is the open claim, \(B_i\) the benchmark family already declared
in \(\mathfrak{T}_{\mathrm{RC},\,\mathrm{bench}}\), \(A_i^{\mathrm{now}}\) the
current computational artifact, \(X_i^{\mathrm{miss}}\) the missing numerical
experiment or benchmark dataset, and \(A_i^{\mathrm{close}}\) the closure
artifact that would count as evidence.  This is the strict continuation of the
logic established in Chapters~4--6: an observable is not merely exported, but
must be connected to a reproducible evidence bundle
\cite{Crisfield1991_NLFEA_Vol1,DeBorst2012_NonlinearFEM}.

\begin{table}[htbp]
  \centering
  \caption{Evidence-closure matrix for the reduced RC column reboot.}
  \label{tab:reduced-rc-column-evidence-closure}
  \scriptsize
  \setlength{\tabcolsep}{3pt}
  \begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{@{}p{0.18\textwidth}p{0.20\textwidth}p{0.20\textwidth}p{0.18\textwidth}X@{}}
    \toprule
    \textbf{Open claim} & \textbf{Current artifact} & \textbf{Missing experiment}
    & \textbf{Closure artifact} & \textbf{Acceptance interpretation} \\
    \midrule
    Runtime reduced-column surface
    & runtime matrix plus audited baseline CSV contracts
    & execute the full \(N \times q\) sweep and summarize finite completion
    & runtime-surface summary table and manifest
    & every declared baseline slice exists and exports the required outputs;
      this closes a runtime completeness obligation, not yet the physical
      benchmark. \\[0.4mm]

    Optional axial-compression path
    & axial-preload branch already running
    & sweep constant axial-load ratios and compare strength/stiffness/dissipation
    & axial-load interaction summary bundle
    & axial-load sensitivity becomes backed by benchmark evidence rather than
      by a single finite smoke run. \\[0.4mm]

    Global hysteresis observable
    & audited hysteresis CSV contract
    & execute the cyclic protocol and compare loop shape, degradation, and
      dissipation against audited reference loops
    & hysteresis comparison bundle
    & the global loop observable becomes a benchmark channel instead of only a
      reproducible export contract. \\[0.4mm]

    Base-side moment-curvature observable
    & \texttt{moment\_curvature\_base.csv} +
      \texttt{moment\_curvature\_closure\_matrix\_summary.csv}
    & freeze the preload-consistent matrix as the internal reference and
      extend the suite toward node-refinement and quadrature-sensitivity
      tables
    & preload-consistent section-comparison bundle +
      refinement/sensitivity bundle
    & the internal reduction error is now jointly bounded in axial force,
      moment, secant stiffness and tangent stiffness over the full runtime
      matrix; what remains open is external benchmark closure. \\[0.4mm]

    Node-refinement convergence
    & full monotonic refinement bundle + full cyclic node-refinement matrix +
      continuation-sensitivity bundle against the highest-\(N\) family reference
    & freeze a declared displacement-control continuation policy, then close
      the remaining cyclic observable-stability question and only escalate to
      arc-length if that extra policy is justified explicitly
    & full cyclic node-refinement bundle + continuation-policy sensitivity note
      + explicit continuation-policy declaration for benchmark closure
    & refinement is already quantified monotonically and over the full cyclic
      matrix; what remains open is not matrix existence but closure of the
      declared base-side observable under a declared continuation policy. \\[0.4mm]

    Quadrature-family sensitivity
    & full monotonic and cyclic family-spread bundles against the
      Gauss--Legendre reference under the declared guarded displacement control
    & freeze the structural reference family, interpret Lobatto/Radau
      departures as explicit station-placement variants, and escalate to
      arc-length only if the chosen reference-family slice still fails for
      reasons beyond placement
    & cyclic quadrature-sensitivity bundle + declared reference-family note +
      station-placement interpretation note
    & family dependence is already bounded monotonically and now measured
      cyclically; what remains open is not bundle existence but the benchmark
      interpretation of family spread under the declared continuation policy. \\
    \bottomrule
  \end{tabularx}
\end{table}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[
      node distance=8mm and 10mm,
      claim/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=blue!5,
                    minimum width=29mm, minimum height=9mm},
      art/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=green!8,
                  minimum width=33mm, minimum height=9mm},
      miss/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=orange!12,
                   minimum width=35mm, minimum height=9mm},
      close/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=red!8,
                    minimum width=34mm, minimum height=9mm},
      arr/.style={-{Latex[length=2.5mm]}, thick}
    ]
    \node[claim] (claim) {Open claim\\\(C_i\)};
    \node[art, right=of claim] (now) {Current artifact\\\(A_i^{\mathrm{now}}\)};
    \node[miss, right=of now] (miss) {Missing experiment\\\(X_i^{\mathrm{miss}}\)};
    \node[close, below=of miss] (close) {Closure artifact\\\(A_i^{\mathrm{close}}\)};

    \draw[arr] (claim) -- (now);
    \draw[arr] (now) -- (miss);
    \draw[arr] (miss) -- (close);
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{The reduced-column campaign now carries a fully explicit
  evidence-closure layer.  This is stricter than a benchmark label alone:
  it says what exists today, what still has to be executed, and what artifact
  would count as closure.}
  \label{fig:reduced-rc-column-evidence-closure}
\end{figure}

Two methodological consequences follow directly.
\begin{enumerate}
  \item The current runtime artifact is not yet evidence of validation.  It is
    only the audited computational substrate from which evidence may later be
    produced.
  \item The same benchmark family can require different evidence classes:
    internal runtime summaries, independent section baselines, or external
    datasets.  The reboot therefore forbids collapsing them into one generic
    label such as ``benchmark completed''.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Canonical reduced-column evidence-closure matrix used by the reboot.},label={lst:reduced-rc-column-evidence-closure}]
constexpr auto evidence =
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_evidence_closure_table_v;

static_assert(evidence.size() == 6);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_evidence_external_dataset_count_v == 2);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_evidence_section_baseline_count_v == 1);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_column_evidence_phase3_gate_count_v == 5);
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection{External computational bridge with OpenSeesPy}
\label{sec:validation-reboot-opensees-bridge}

The reboot now carries one additional layer between the internal
\texttt{fall\_n} artifacts and the later physical/literature benchmark
closure: an \emph{external computational reference} built in OpenSeesPy through
\texttt{scripts/opensees\_reduced\_rc\_column\_reference.py}.  The rationale is
methodological, not cosmetic.  Before the reduced-column campaign is promoted
to experimental closure, it is valuable to compare the same structural object
against an independently implemented beam-column stack based on the
OpenSees/OpenSeesPy ecosystem
\cite{OpenSeesWebsite,OpenSeesPyDocs,Scott2008_SoftwarePatternsBeamColumnModels,Li2013_FiberSectionTimoshenkoElementOpenSees}.

This bridge is intentionally defined as
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{M}_{\texttt{fall\_n}}^{\mathrm{red}}
  \not\equiv
  \mathcal{M}_{\texttt{OpenSees}}^{\mathrm{bridge}},
\end{equation}
not because the comparison is weak, but because it is honest.  The OpenSeesPy
route no longer hides a single hard-coded external constitutive translation;
instead it exposes a small declared policy surface:
\texttt{monotonic-reference} (no-tension \texttt{Concrete02} plus baseline
\texttt{Steel02}), \texttt{cyclic-diagnostic} (reduced-tension
\texttt{Concrete02} plus tuned \texttt{Steel02} from the uniaxial audit), and
\texttt{elasticized-parity}.  The current \texttt{fall\_n} reduced-column path
remains anchored to the audited Kent--Park / Menegotto ingredient family.  The
bridge therefore compares \emph{observables under a shared benchmark
specification} rather than claiming parameter-by-parameter constitutive
identity.

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[
      node distance=8mm and 10mm,
      spec/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=blue!5,
                   minimum width=31mm, minimum height=9mm},
      run/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=green!8,
                  minimum width=34mm, minimum height=9mm},
      compare/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=orange!12,
                      minimum width=36mm, minimum height=9mm},
      close/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, fill=red!8,
                    minimum width=36mm, minimum height=9mm},
      arr/.style={-{Latex[length=2.5mm]}, thick}
    ]
    \node[spec] (spec) {Shared benchmark\\specification};
    \node[run, right=of spec] (falln) {\texttt{fall\_n}\\reduced slice};
    \node[run, below=of falln] (ops) {OpenSeesPy\\external bridge};
    \node[compare, right=of falln] (cmp) {Observable-level\\comparison bundle};
    \node[close, right=of cmp] (phys) {Later physical /\\literature closure};

    \draw[arr] (spec) -- (falln);
    \draw[arr] (spec) |- (ops);
    \draw[arr] (falln) -- (cmp);
    \draw[arr] (ops) -- (cmp);
    \draw[arr] (cmp) -- (phys);
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{Role of the OpenSeesPy bridge in the rebooted campaign.  It is an
  external computational comparator for the same reduced-column specification,
  not a replacement for later physical/literature closure.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-opensees-bridge}
\end{figure}

The benchmark specification shared by both routes is intentionally the same
one already frozen by the reduced-column reboot: same column geometry, same
axial preload level, same beam-integration family and number of stations, and
the same monotonic or cyclic tip-displacement protocol.  The script writes a
machine-readable bundle with
\texttt{reference\_manifest.json}, \texttt{hysteresis.csv},
\texttt{section\_response.csv}, and \texttt{moment\_curvature\_base.csv}, so the
comparison surface is aligned with the \texttt{fall\_n} validation artifacts.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash,caption={Representative OpenSeesPy bridge invocation for the reduced RC-column reboot.},label={lst:validation-reboot-opensees-bridge-run}]
py -3.12 scripts/opensees_reduced_rc_column_reference.py \
  --analysis cyclic \
  --mapping-policy cyclic-diagnostic \
  --beam-element-family disp \
  --beam-integration legendre \
  --integration-points 3 \
  --geom-transf linear \
  --axial-compression-mn 0.02 \
  --amplitudes-mm 1.25 \
  --steps-per-segment 1 \
  --reversal-substep-factor 2 \
  --max-bisections 4 \
  --output-dir data/output/cyclic_validation/reboot_opensees_reference_cyclic_smoke
\end{lstlisting}

The campaign now also has a unified computational benchmark runner:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash,caption={Canonical \texttt{fall\_n} vs OpenSeesPy benchmark invocation for the reduced reference slice.},label={lst:validation-reboot-external-benchmark-run}]
python scripts/run_reduced_rc_column_external_benchmark.py \
  --analysis cyclic \
  --mapping-policy cyclic-diagnostic \
  --beam-nodes 4 \
  --beam-integration legendre \
  --beam-element-family disp \
  --geom-transf linear \
  --axial-compression-mn 0.02 \
  --amplitudes-mm 1.25 \
  --steps-per-segment 1 \
  --reversal-substep-factor 2 \
  --max-bisections 4 \
  --output-dir data/output/cyclic_validation/reboot_external_benchmark_cyclic_bc_audit
\end{lstlisting}

This runner is methodologically important because it closes the last tooling
gap between the internal reduced-column slice and the external computational
bridge.  The bundle now freezes, in one place,
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the \texttt{fall\_n} runtime manifest,
  \item the OpenSeesPy reference manifest,
  \item the preload/control trace on both sides,
  \item the observable-level comparison summary, and
  \item the auxiliary compute-time summary.
\end{enumerate}

The first short cyclic bundle is already informative.  After correcting a real
unit-consistency error in the original OpenSeesPy bridge (geometry and loads in
\(m\) and \(N\), but concrete/steel still passed in \(MPa\) instead of \(Pa\)),
the benchmark now completes cleanly on both sides for the reference slice
\((N=4,\ \text{Gauss-Legendre},\ 0.02\,\text{MN axial compression},\
1.25\,\text{mm amplitude})\).  A third parity issue also had to be fixed:
the external structural bridge had been anchored on \texttt{forceBeamColumn}
with a \texttt{PDelta} transformation, whereas the current \texttt{fall\_n}
reduced-column slice is a small-strain displacement-based beam benchmark.  The
reference structural bridge is now anchored on
\texttt{dispBeamColumn + LinearCrdTransf}.  Under that declared
\texttt{cyclic-diagnostic} policy, \texttt{fall\_n} reports about
\(1.99\times 10^{-1}\,\text{s}\) total wall time, whereas OpenSeesPy reports
about \(2.16\times 10^{-1}\,\text{s}\).  This timing read is intentionally
auxiliary: it characterizes computational cost, but it does not replace the
mechanical acceptance gate.

The mechanical result is the real message. A second benchmark bug was found and
corrected here as well: the exported OpenSees base-shear observable had been
using the opposite reaction sign convention from the one already used by
\texttt{fall\_n}. Once that convention is aligned, and once the beam
formulation is moved to the displacement-based parity anchor, the short
structural bundle becomes much more informative.  The compared history now
spans the full \(13\) sampled points of the guarded displacement path, not
only the turning points. On the active cyclic points,
\[
\max \varepsilon_{V} \approx 2.18\times 10^{-1},\qquad
\operatorname{rms}\varepsilon_{V} \approx 1.90\times 10^{-1},\qquad
\max \varepsilon_{M} \approx 2.33\times 10^{-1},\qquad
\operatorname{rms}\varepsilon_{M} \approx 1.96\times 10^{-1}.
\]
That is an honest and useful result. It means the benchmark is no longer
dominated by an orientation error: base shear and base moment-curvature are now
misaligned mainly in amplitude, not in sign. Moreover, the benchmark now emits
an explicit spatial-parity audit: both sides use the same \(92\) fiber
centroids, the same tributary areas, the same concrete/steel zone labels, and
the same three Gauss--Legendre section stations within roundoff
\((\sim10^{-10}\text{--}10^{-12})\).  The policy seam is therefore already
scientifically valuable, but closure has still not been reached.

The new boundary-condition audit removes another potential false culprit.  On
the same short cyclic slice, the actual tip drift closes essentially at machine
precision,
\[
\max \varepsilon_{u_x}^{\text{ctrl}} \approx 6.94\times10^{-16},
\]
and the maintained base axial reaction closes essentially exactly as well,
\[
\max \varepsilon_{R_z}^{\text{ctrl}} \approx 2.50\times10^{-8}.
\]
So the residual structural gap is \emph{not} coming from a mismatch in the
gradual displacement-control path or from loss of the constant axial load
during the lateral branch.  What does not close is the preload deformation
state itself: at the preload-equilibrated point, \texttt{fall\_n} predicts
about \(-2.92\times10^{-5}\,\text{m}\) top axial shortening, whereas OpenSees
predicts about \(-4.35\times10^{-5}\,\text{m}\).  The same discrepancy is
already visible in the mean section preload state
\((\bar{\varepsilon}_{\text{ax}} \approx -9.12\times10^{-6}\) versus
\(-1.36\times10^{-5})\) and in the mean preload flexural tangent
\((\bar{EI}_y \approx 11.74\) versus \(9.62)\).  This is a much stronger and
more useful diagnosis: the bridge is now limited mainly by nonlinear
section/preload response, not by boundary-condition enforcement.

The next task is therefore not to make the benchmark run, but to reduce that
remaining nonlinear modeling gap before promoting this bridge to a normative
comparison aid.

The new structural bundle also carries a station-by-station section-path
comparison over the same three Gauss--Legendre stations.  That matters because
the residual structural discrepancy can now be localized within the distributed
section history instead of being inferred only from the global loop.  On the
current short cyclic slice, the distributed comparison yields
\[
\max \varepsilon_{M}^{\text{sec,path}} \approx 3.40\times10^{-1},\qquad
\operatorname{rms}\varepsilon_{M}^{\text{sec,path}} \approx 2.09\times10^{-1},
\]
\[
\max \varepsilon_{\kappa}^{\text{sec,path}} \approx 1.96\times10^{-1},\qquad
\operatorname{rms}\varepsilon_{\kappa}^{\text{sec,path}} \approx 6.15\times10^{-2},
\]
\[
\max \varepsilon_{K_t}^{\text{sec,path}} \approx 1.47\times10^{0},\qquad
\operatorname{rms}\varepsilon_{K_t}^{\text{sec,path}} \approx 3.80\times10^{-1},
\]
with axial-force drift still secondary at this level,
\[
\max \varepsilon_{N}^{\text{sec,path}} \approx 7.47\times10^{-2}.
\]
The spatial signature is already informative: the loaded-end station
(\texttt{gp = 2}) drives the largest moment/curvature discrepancy, whereas the
base station (\texttt{gp = 0}) drives the largest tangent discrepancy.  The
