included, \(18\) enriched host nodes, \(309\) local state DOFs, and \(197\)
reduced solver DOFs after Dirichlet elimination.  The same eight longitudinal
bars used by the fiber section are represented by \(32\) two-node
Menegotto--Pinto truss elements.  Their interior nodes are tied to the enriched
host interpolation by \(24\) penalty constraints of the form
\[
  \mathbf{g}_r =
  \mathbf{u}_r
  - \sum_I N_I(\mathbf{x}_r)\mathbf{u}_I
  - \sum_{I\in\mathcal{E}_{\mathrm{XFEM}}}
    N_I(\mathbf{x}_r)
    \bigl[H(\phi(\mathbf{x}_r))-H(\phi(\mathbf{x}_I))\bigr]\mathbf{a}_I ,
\]
so the rebar sees the same displacement jump as the cut solid instead of
slipping through an unenriched host.  The crack is placed at
\(z=0.1\,\mathrm{m}\), inside the first biased layer, and the cyclic drift
protocol up to \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) is imposed on the top face while a
\(0.02\,\mathrm{MN}\) axial compression is applied as a Neumann load.

Two global material branches are now retained.  The elastic-host control
converges the full \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) protocol in about \(12\,\mathrm{s}\),
reaches \(|V_b|_{\max}\approx0.318\,\mathrm{MN}\), and drives the coupled steel
to \(\sigma_s\approx456\,\mathrm{MPa}\).  The promoted nonlinear-control branch
uses \texttt{ComponentwiseKentParkConcrete3D}, i.e. the same uniaxial
Kent--Park tension/compression law used by the structural fibers applied to the
three normal Voigt components, plus elastic shear.  With the typed SNES
cascade active, this branch completes the same \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) protocol in
\(\sim111\,\mathrm{s}\), reaches \(|V_b|_{\max}\approx0.0224\,\mathrm{MN}\),
\(\sigma_s\approx489\,\mathrm{MPa}\), and reports \(64\) damaged host material
points.  This is the first global XFEM+truss+nonlinear-concrete local model
that reaches the target amplitude.  The more aggressive
\texttt{CyclicCrackBandConcrete3D} branch remains diagnostic: it cracks and
degrades the host too abruptly near \(2\)--\(3\,\mathrm{mm}\) for the current
Newton path, so it should be revisited with a consistent softening tangent or
arc-length/continuation before promotion.

That revisit has now started in code rather than only in prose.  The
\texttt{CyclicCrackBandConcrete3D} relation exposes a selectable tangent policy:
a production-oriented positive secant tangent, an adaptive central-difference
tangent, and a central-difference tangent with secant fallback.  The consistent
tangent is verified against an independent finite-difference regression and
does capture negative tensile-softening stiffness.  In the current global XFEM
column, however, this extra information is not yet a free win: on the smallest
\(2\,\mathrm{mm}\) smoke cycle it produces essentially the same response as the
secant tangent but raises the runtime from about \(0.53\,\mathrm{s}\) to about
\(33\)--\(35\,\mathrm{s}\) because every material tangent evaluation performs
multiple stress calls and the onset surface is still non-smooth.  The
engineering interpretation is therefore conservative: keep the central tangent
as a constitutive audit and future continuation ingredient, while retaining the
secant tangent as the default global XFEM path until an analytic or active-set
consistent tangent is available.  In parallel, \texttt{ArcLengthSolver} now
accepts the same local residual, reduced global residual and Jacobian hooks as
\texttt{NonlinearAnalysis}; this prevents future continuation studies from
silently dropping enriched rebar--host penalty terms when the XFEM model is
run outside pure displacement control.  The \texttt{steppable\_solver}
regression now executes a one-step total-Lagrangian arc-length solve and checks
that all three hook channels are called.

With that default, the aggressive crack-band host now completes a coarse global
XFEM smoke run all the way to the \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) cyclic protocol.  The
diagnostic mesh uses \(1\times1\times2\) Hex8 host cells plus the eight
Menegotto--Pinto truss bars coupled to the shifted-Heaviside host.  It reaches
\(|V_b|_{\max}\approx0.0261\,\mathrm{MN}\),
\(\sigma_s^{\max}\approx432\,\mathrm{MPa}\), \(d_{\max}=0.98\), and completes
in about \(21\,\mathrm{s}\).  This is not a mesh-converged local model; it is a
useful algorithmic gate showing that the coupled XFEM/truss/crack-band chain
can survive the full target amplitude before the next refinement and physics
closure pass.

The first direct structural comparison was then launched with the same
\(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) protocol.  The reference structural run uses
\(N=10\) Lobatto stations, the fine section-fiber profile
\((336\) concrete fibers plus eight steel fibers), axial preload
\(0.02\,\mathrm{MN}\), and the declared reversal-guarded continuation policy.
It completes with \(145\) hysteresis points in about \(243\,\mathrm{s}\).  A
matching XFEM smoke run was repeated with \(145\) points so that comparison can
be performed over the same protocol pseudo-time.  The raw comparison exposes a
base-reaction convention difference: the structural and global-XFEM base shear
have opposite signs.  After applying the documented sign factor
\(-1\) to the structural reaction, the peak-normalized RMS base-shear gap is
\(7.39\times10^{-2}\), the peak-normalized maximum gap is
\(1.99\times10^{-1}\), and the XFEM-to-structural peak ratio is \(1.107\).
This is not yet physical closure, because the XFEM mesh is deliberately coarse
and the crack is still fixed as a single base plane.  It is, however, the first
quantitative evidence that the secant crack-band XFEM branch is in the same
global force scale as the high-resolution structural reference.

The first XFEM mesh-refinement matrix then separated two effects that had been
implicitly tied together in the initial smoke runs: the longitudinal host mesh
and the physical crack-plane location.  The benchmark driver now accepts
\texttt{--global-xfem-crack-z-m}; when this value is prescribed, it must lie
strictly inside an element rather than on a grid level, avoiding a degenerate
shifted-Heaviside split.  For the refinement audit the crack plane was held at
\(z_c=0.60\,\mathrm{m}\) while the host mesh was varied uniformly and with
fixed-end bias.  Four cases completed the \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) cyclic protocol
with \texttt{CyclicCrackBandConcrete3D} and the production secant tangent.  The
best finished case was the \(2\times2\times2\) fixed-end-biased Hex8 host:
\(95\) reduced PETSc DOFs, \(24\) host elements, \(18\) enriched host nodes,
\(68\,\mathrm{s}\) wall time, peak-normalized RMS base-shear gap
\(9.59\times10^{-2}\), and peak-normalized maximum gap \(2.86\times10^{-1}\).
The \(1\times1\times4\) uniform branch reached a similar RMS gap
\(9.78\times10^{-2}\) but needed \(114\,\mathrm{s}\), while the \(2\times2\times2\)
uniform branch over-stiffened the peak response.  The single-cell biased
branches and the \(2\times2\times4\) biased branch timed out under the present
secant Newton cascade, which is a solver/localization warning rather than a
physical conclusion.

This audit changes the interpretation of the earlier coarse result.  XFEM is
indeed much closer to the structural reference than the basic smeared-continuum
branch, but mesh refinement alone is not yet monotone because the single
prescribed crack plane controls hinge length, steel work, and concrete
dissipation.  The next closure step is therefore a small physical
calibration/convergence matrix over \(z_c\), cohesive fracture energy and
opening-dependent shear transfer, not an indiscriminate increase of host DOFs.

\paragraph{Promotion gate toward the multiscale local model.}
The route to the multiscale stage is now frozen as a code-level promotion
matrix rather than as prose only.  The header
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCLocalModelPromotionCatalog.hh} separates five
roles:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the \(N=10\) Lobatto structural fiber-section column, which is the
    internal physical reference but not a local multiscale model;
  \item the standard smeared-crack continuum with Dirichlet rebar end caps and
    composite axial preload split, which is a promoted regression control;
  \item the shifted-Heaviside XFEM global column, which is the primary
    multiscale local-model candidate;
  \item Ko--Bathe Hex20/Hex27 continua, retained as heavier physics
    guardrails; and
  \item OpenSees continuum runs, retained as external comparison controls.
\end{enumerate}
This classification matters because each object answers a different scientific
question.  The structural model defines the target loop and the section-level
steel/concrete physics.  The standard continuum checks load transfer, axial
resultants, host--bar compatibility and external solver parity.  The XFEM
branch is the only current candidate allowed to close the localized-fracture
gap, but it must pass a stricter promotion gate before being used as the local
model in FE\textsuperscript{2}.

The current gate is deliberately quantitative.  A candidate XFEM branch must
complete the \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) protocol, keep the peak-normalized RMS
base-shear error below \(0.10\), keep the peak-normalized maximum error below
\(0.30\), keep the XFEM/structural peak base-shear ratio in
\([0.90,1.15]\), drive the steel into the Menegotto--Pinto yield range, and
complete the declared refinement matrix without unresolved timeouts.  These
numbers are not universal material constants; they are the present
engineering acceptance band for deciding whether the local model is close
enough to enter multiscale calibration.  The runner
\texttt{scripts/run\_xfem\_structural\_refinement\_matrix.py} now writes this
promotion decision explicitly into the JSON summary as a
\texttt{promotion\_gate} block, so a visually plausible hysteresis loop cannot
silently override failed mesh or continuation cases.

\paragraph{Unit-consistent XFEM cohesive closure update.}
The first closure attempt after defining the promotion gate exposed a genuine
unit inconsistency in the enriched crack surface.  The local cohesive-hinge
surrogate evaluates crack openings in millimetres, whereas the global
shifted-Heaviside solid obtains the crack jump directly from nodal
displacements in metres.  Reusing the same cohesive parameter object in both
places therefore shifted the interface stiffness and critical opening by
orders of magnitude.  The implementation now separates the two cases:
\texttt{make\_crack\_band\_consistent\_cohesive\_law} is retained for
millimetre-based section/hyper-surface calculations, while
\texttt{make\_metre\_jump\_crack\_band\_consistent\_cohesive\_law\_from\_mpa\_n\_per\_mm}
converts the concrete fracture energy from \(N/mm\) to \(MN/m\) and uses
\(l_c\) in metres.  Consequently
\[
  K_n = {E_c\over l_c},\qquad
  G_f^{MN/m}=10^{-3}G_f^{N/mm},\qquad
  \delta_f = {2G_f^{MN/m}\over f_t},
\]
with \(\delta_f\) expressed in metres for the global XFEM element.

This correction made the interface physically sharper but also revealed why
the old secant branch was numerically forgiving: the global crack surface had
been inadvertently too ductile.  To keep the corrected interface usable in
Newton iterations, the cohesive response now exposes a selectable tangent
policy.  The default production matrix uses a central-difference tangent with
secant fallback for the cohesive surface, while the secant-positive tangent
remains available as a robust diagnostic.  In addition, the tangential
crack-transfer cap was moved inside the cohesive law instead of being applied
only as a local post-processing clamp.  This is important because the same
limited shear-transfer law now enters the residual, the tangent and the base
reaction.

The current best cheap global run uses the \(1\times1\times2\) Hex8 host mesh,
the corrected metre-jump cohesive law, central-fallback cohesive tangent and a
small open-crack shear cap of \(0.05\,\mathrm{MPa}\).  It completes the
\(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) cyclic protocol without timeout, reaches steel yielding
\((\sigma_s^{max}\approx429\,\mathrm{MPa})\), and matches the peak base shear
well:
\[
  {|V_b|^{XFEM}_{max}\over |V_b|^{str}_{max}}\approx1.046.
\]
However, it is not yet promoted: the sign-aligned peak-normalized RMS error is
still about \(0.182\), the maximum normalized error about \(0.376\), and the
loop work remains too small
\((W_{XFEM}\approx9.07\ \mathrm{MN\,mm}\) versus
\(W_{str}\approx15.06\ \mathrm{MN\,mm})\).  The gap is therefore no longer a
trivial reaction sign, axial-load split, steel area or peak-capacity error.  It
is a cyclic-memory/localization error: the global XFEM bar discretization still
spreads crack-crossing steel deformation over long truss segments, and the
cohesive crack law has damage and shear cap but not yet a full hysteretic
bond-slip/frictional memory.

The next closure iteration therefore introduced a separate crack-crossing
reinforcement bridge, not as a hidden correction inside the benchmark but as a
finite element with its own uniaxial constitutive state:
\texttt{src/xfem/ShiftedHeavisideCrackCrossingRebarElement.hh}.  At a crack
surface point \(\xi_c\), it reads only the enriched displacement jump,
\[
  \jump{u}(\xi_c)=
  2\sum_{I\in\mathcal{E}_{\mathrm{XFEM}}}N_I(\xi_c)a_I,
\]
and projects that jump onto a selected reinforcement bridge direction
\(\mathbf e_b\),
\[
  s_b = \mathbf e_b\cdot \jump{u}(\xi_c),\qquad
  \varepsilon_b ={s_b\over l_g}.
\]
For the material-backed audit law, the Menegotto--Pinto response is evaluated
with \(\varepsilon_b\), but the virtual work is written in terms of the
localized slip \(s_b\).  Thus the global residual and tangent use
\[
  f_b = A_b\,\sigma_b(\varepsilon_b)\,G_b^T,\qquad
  K_b = {A_b\,E_{t,b}(\varepsilon_b)\over l_g}\,G_b^T G_b,
\]
with \(G_b=\partial s_b/\partial a\).  Because this is a real
element, not a nonlinear-analysis hook, it participates in the same
PETSc/SNES assembly, material commit and rollback semantics as the ordinary
truss family.  The bridge is disabled by default in the executable
\((A_b^{eff}=0)\) so the unit-consistent XFEM baseline remains reproducible;
calibration studies opt in through
\texttt{--global-xfem-crack-crossing-rebar-mode} and
\texttt{--global-xfem-crack-crossing-rebar-area-scale}.

The first exploratory calibration separates two mechanisms.  An axial bridge
aligned with the column axis does not recover the missing loop area once the
cyclic crack-band concrete host is active, which suggests that the remaining
error is not controlled by normal crack opening alone.  A tangential
\texttt{dowel-x} bridge is more influential: with
\(\alpha_A=A_b^{eff}/A_b=0.001\), the same \(1\times1\times2\) XFEM column
reaches \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) in about \(25.4\,\mathrm{s}\), improves the
peak-normalized RMS error from \(0.182\) to \(0.159\), and increases the loop
work from \(9.07\) to \(10.54\,\mathrm{MN\,mm}\).  Larger dowel scales can
approach or exceed the structural loop work, but they over-stiffen the peak
response and produce very high equivalent dowel stresses.  This is important:
the next physical model should be a bounded dowel or bond-slip transfer law,
not another area-scale calibration knob.

That bounded law is now implemented as an alternative constitutive policy for
the same crack-crossing element.  It acts directly on slip, not on an artificial
steel strain, through a one-dimensional return map
\[
  F_b^{tr}=k_0(s_b-s_p),\qquad
  \Phi=\left|F_b^{tr}-\beta\right|-F_y\le0,
\]
where \(s_p\) is the committed plastic slip, \(\beta\) a linear kinematic
back-force and \(F_y\) the per-bridge transfer capacity.  If
\(\Phi>0\),
\[
  \Delta\gamma={\Phi\over k_0+H},\qquad
  s_p^{n+1}=s_p^n+\Delta\gamma\,\mathrm{sign}(F_b^{tr}-\beta),\qquad
  \beta^{n+1}=\beta^n+H\Delta\gamma\,\mathrm{sign}(F_b^{tr}-\beta),
\]
and the algorithmic tangent is \(k_0H/(k_0+H)\), optionally clipped by a
force cap \(F_{\max}\).  This is deliberately modest physics: it does not
pretend to be a full dowel-bearing or ribbed-bar bond-slip model, but it gives
the enriched crack a bounded, history-aware steel transfer mechanism with the
same PETSc assembly path as every other element.  In the code it is selected by
\texttt{--global-xfem-crack-crossing-bridge-law bounded-slip}; the direct
Menegotto--Pinto strain bridge remains available only as an audit/control
branch.

The promoted first local-model closure uses a \(1\times1\times4\) uniform Hex8
XFEM host, the fixed physical crack plane \(z_c=0.60\,\mathrm{m}\), the
metre-consistent cyclic crack-band cohesive law with central-fallback tangent,
an open-crack shear cap of \(0.02\,\mathrm{MPa}\), and eight
\texttt{dowel-x} bounded-slip bridge elements with
\[
  F_y=F_{\max}=1.90\times10^{-3}\,\mathrm{MN},\qquad
  s_y=0.25\,\mathrm{mm}.
\]
Against the \(N=10\) Lobatto structural reference it completes all \(97\)
protocol points up to \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The sign-aligned metrics are
\[
  { |V_b|^{XFEM}_{max}\over |V_b|^{str}_{max}}=1.149,\qquad
  e_{RMS}^{norm}=0.082,\qquad
  e_{max}^{norm}=0.262,
\]
with \(W_{XFEM}=15.76\,\mathrm{MN\,mm}\) versus
\(W_{str}=15.06\,\mathrm{MN\,mm}\), peak steel stress
\(\sigma_s^{max}\approx437\,\mathrm{MPa}\), and maximum host damage \(0.98\).
These values pass the current promotion gate
\((e_{RMS}^{norm}<0.10,\ e_{max}^{norm}<0.30,\ 0.90\le
|V_b|^{XFEM}_{max}/|V_b|^{str}_{max}\le1.15)\).  The local-model promotion
catalog therefore marks this branch as the first
\texttt{promoted\_physical\_local\_model}; it is eligible for the next
multiscale stage, while the remaining work is production robustness rather
than basic structural--local equivalence.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Compile-time promotion gate for the reduced RC local-model campaign.},label={lst:validation-reboot-local-model-promotion-catalog}]
constexpr auto rows =
  fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_local_model_promotion_table_v;

static_assert(
  fall_n::canonical_reduced_rc_primary_multiscale_candidate_count_v == 1);

constexpr auto xfem =
  fall_n::find_reduced_rc_local_model_promotion_row(
    rows, "xfem_global_secant_200mm_primary_candidate");

static_assert(xfem.requires_enriched_dofs);
static_assert(xfem.criteria.max_peak_normalized_rms_base_shear_error <= 0.10);
\end{lstlisting}

The remaining scientific step is now narrower and better defined: preserve
this promoted baseline as the multiscale-entry candidate, then harden it for
production.  A first tangent-policy benchmark separates solver policy from
physical response.  The \texttt{central-fallback} cohesive tangent remains the
robust canonical reference: it completes the promoted \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\)
case in \(90.5\,\mathrm{s}\), with \(1441\) accumulated Newton iterations and
one hard step reaching the iteration cap.  The pure \texttt{secant} tangent
keeps the same hysteresis metrics and is faster in wall time
\((80.4\,\mathrm{s})\), but it uses more accumulated Newton iterations
\((1918)\) and four hard steps.  The current analytic \texttt{active-set}
tangent is therefore not promoted: it preserves the physical curve, but needs
\(161\,\mathrm{s}\), \(2003\) accumulated Newton iterations and five hard
steps.  The next robustness work should focus on arc-length and non-Newton
continuation around crack-state changes, adaptive crack-plane
placement/refinement, and only then a second-generation active-set tangent.

The dedicated regression also drives one cut Hex8 through PETSc/SNES under
displacement control, converging a two-step solve with the enriched DOFs
active.  This gives the first end-to-end nonlinear-solver gate for the global
XFEM element; further production work should continue on this same path rather
than returning to an uncoupled surrogate.

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_local_cohesive_hinge_200mm_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{First XFEM local cohesive-hinge hysteresis benchmark up to
  \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The promoted branch isolates flexural crack opening
  and steel crossing the enriched crack plane.  The dashed sensitivity branch
  shows why direct crack-plane shear transfer cannot yet be promoted without a
  richer shear-slip/contact law.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-local-hinge-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_global_componentwise_kp_cascade_200mm_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{Full PETSc/SNES shifted-Heaviside XFEM reinforced-column trial up to
  \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\), overlaid with the local reinforced cohesive-hinge
  surrogate.  The global branch now includes Menegotto--Pinto truss bars tied
  to the enriched host and a componentwise Kent--Park concrete control law.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-global-newton-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_global_cyclic_crack_band_secant_200mm_smoke_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{Coarse global XFEM smoke run with
  \texttt{CyclicCrackBandConcrete3D} and secant tangent up to
  \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The run is an algorithmic survival check for the
  enriched solid, truss coupling and crack-band host, not yet a
  mesh-converged physical closure against the structural reference.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-global-crack-band-smoke-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering

  secant crack-band branch and the \(N=10\) Lobatto structural reference up to
  \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The structural base reaction is sign-aligned for this
  plot; the raw sign convention is retained in the JSON summary.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-secant-vs-structural-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_global_secant_structural_refinement_matrix_200mm.png}
  \caption{Global XFEM secant mesh-refinement matrix with a fixed physical
  crack plane at \(z_c=0.60\,\mathrm{m}\), compared against the \(N=10\)
  Lobatto structural reference up to \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The best completed
  branch is the \(2\times2\times2\) fixed-end-biased host; timed-out biased
  refinements are retained in the JSON failure markers rather than promoted as
  converged results.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-secant-refinement-matrix-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_unit_consistent_central_cap0p05_vs_structural_200mm_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{Unit-consistent global XFEM comparison against the structural
  \(N=10\) Lobatto reference.  The corrected cohesive surface uses metre-based
  jumps, central-fallback interface tangent and a \(0.05\,\mathrm{MPa}\)
  open-crack shear-transfer cap.  Peak strength and steel yielding are now in
  the right band, but the loop remains too pinched; the remaining closure must
  target crack-crossing reinforcement localization and hysteretic interface
  memory.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-unit-consistent-cap005-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_ccb_dowelx_scale0001_1x1x2_vs_structural_200mm_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{Exploratory crack-crossing dowel bridge in the global XFEM branch
  (\(\alpha_A=0.001\), \(l_g=100\,\mathrm{mm}\), \texttt{dowel-x}).  The
  additional bridge improves the sign-aligned RMS error and adds cyclic memory,
  but it is not promoted because the maximum normalized error remains above the
  gate and the equivalent dowel stress is too high.  The result is evidence
  for a bounded dowel/bond-slip law rather than for direct area scaling.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-dowel-bridge-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_ccb_bounded_dowelx_nz4_cap0p020_fy0p00190_vs_structural_200mm_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{Promoted bounded-dowel global XFEM local baseline against the
  \(N=10\) Lobatto structural reference up to \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The case
  uses a \(1\times1\times4\) Hex8 host, fixed crack plane
  \(z_c=0.60\,\mathrm{m}\), \(0.02\,\mathrm{MPa}\) cohesive shear cap and
  \texttt{dowel-x} bounded-slip bridges with
  \(F_y=F_{\max}=1.90\times10^{-3}\,\mathrm{MN}\) per bridge.  It passes the
  promotion gate with peak-normalized RMS \(0.082\), maximum normalized error
  \(0.262\), peak ratio \(1.149\), and loop work close to the structural
  reference.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-bounded-dowel-promoted-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_promoted_bounded_dowel_refinement_matrix_200mm.png}
  \caption{Promoted-parameter bounded-dowel XFEM refinement matrix.  The complete uniform
  refinements show that longitudinal resolution improves the RMS response,
  while transverse refinement can over-strengthen the local model for the
  current bridge and cohesive parameters.  With the promoted
  \(F_y=F_{\max}=1.90\times10^{-3}\,\mathrm{MN}\) bridge law, the
  \(1\times1\times4\) uniform branch is the only member of this small matrix
  that passes all response gates.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-bounded-dowel-refinement-matrix-200mm}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_promoted_bounded_dowel_tangent_policy_benchmark_200mm.png}
  \caption{Cohesive tangent-policy benchmark on the promoted bounded-dowel
  XFEM local model.  The physical response is unchanged to plotting precision,
  but the nonlinear work changes substantially.  The central-fallback tangent
  is retained as the robust canonical reference, the secant tangent is an
  accelerated candidate, and the current active-set tangent is negative
  evidence until the continuation strategy is improved.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-bounded-dowel-tangent-policy-200mm}
\end{figure}

The nonlinear-solver benchmark then froze the promoted physical model and
changed only the PETSc/SNES profile.  This is the right separation: if the
hysteresis changes, the physical model changed; if the cost and failure modes
change while the hysteresis is invariant, the solver policy is being measured.
Two profiles complete the full \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) protocol.  Newton with the
L2 line search is the fastest completed direct profile
\((81.2\,\mathrm{s}, 1433\) accumulated nonlinear iterations), while the typed
Newton cascade is slightly slower but more robust
\((94.1\,\mathrm{s}, 1441\) iterations, fewer failed attempts and one hard
requested step).  Pure backtracking, pure trust-region, dogleg,
quasi-Newton, nonlinear GMRES, Anderson acceleration and nonlinear conjugate
gradient are not promoted as direct replacements on this branch: some fail at
the first crack-state transition, and NCG times out under the current
configuration.

This result also clarifies the role of arc-length.  The existing
\texttt{ArcLengthSolver} is a load-proportional continuation route, but the
promoted XFEM benchmark is driven by imposed cyclic Dirichlet displacements at
the column tip.  A scientifically honest arc-length closure for this case
cannot be a one-line replacement for SNES; it must be a bordered or mixed
control continuation carrying the imposed displacement, load reaction and
enriched crack-state variables in the same augmented system.  Until that is
implemented, the multiscale-entry default should be the typed Newton cascade,
with Newton--L2 retained as the faster production candidate when the step
history remains regular.

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_promoted_bounded_dowel_solver_policy_benchmark_200mm.png}
  \caption{PETSc nonlinear-solver policy benchmark on the promoted
  bounded-dowel XFEM local model.  The physical hysteresis is unchanged for
  completed runs; the algorithmic cost and robustness are not.  Newton--L2 is
  the fastest completed profile, while the typed Newton cascade is retained as
  the more robust multiscale-entry default.  Direct non-Newton profiles are
  negative evidence until a mixed-control continuation layer is introduced.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-bounded-dowel-solver-policy-200mm}
\end{figure}

The first mixed-control continuation layer is now implemented rather than left
as a slogan.  The new
\texttt{src/analysis/MixedControlArcLengthContinuation.hh} wrapper is built on
the checkpointable \texttt{SteppableSolver} contract: it advances an imposed
Dirichlet protocol with \texttt{step\_to}, samples user-declared observables,
and rolls the solver back if a numerically converged step exceeds the scaled
mixed arc
\[
  \|\Delta q\|_{\mathrm{mix}}^2 =
  w_u\left(\frac{\Delta u_c}{u_0}\right)^2+
  w_R\left(\frac{\Delta R_b}{R_0}\right)^2+
  w_d\left(\frac{\Delta d}{d_0}\right)^2 .
\]
For the reduced-column XFEM benchmark \(u_c\) is the top-face drift, \(R_b\)
is the base shear and \(d\) is the maximum host damage.  Protocol guard points
are passed to the driver, so the adaptive continuation may subdivide a segment
but may not jump over a reversal point or miss the declared \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\)
peak.  This is still not the final bordered Newton system; it is the honest
mixed-control continuation seam needed by the present Dirichlet-driven local
model.

The second-generation bordered Newton layer is no longer only a mathematical
sketch.  The small algebraic contract in
\texttt{src/analysis/BorderedMixedControlNewton.hh} is now mirrored by
\texttt{src/analysis/PetscBorderedMixedControlNewton.hh}, which assembles and
solves the explicit PETSc system
\begin{equation}
  \begin{bmatrix}
    K & r_{\lambda}\\
    g^{T} & c_{\lambda}
  \end{bmatrix}
  \begin{bmatrix}
    \Delta u\\
    \Delta \lambda
  \end{bmatrix}
  =
  -
  \begin{bmatrix}
    R\\
    c
  \end{bmatrix}.
\end{equation}
Here \(R\) is the equilibrium residual, \(K\) the tangent, \(r_\lambda\)
the load/control column, \(c\) the scalar mixed-control constraint, \(g\) its
gradient with respect to the unknowns and \(c_\lambda\) its derivative with
respect to the load/control parameter.  This separation is intentional:
the physics callback remains outside the linear algebra layer, while the
bordered solve itself is now tested with PETSc \texttt{Mat}/\texttt{Vec}/
\texttt{KSP}.  Therefore the open task has narrowed: the next XFEM benchmark
step is not to invent the bordered algebra.  The SNES assembly route now also
has a public trial-evaluation seam in \texttt{NonlinearAnalysis}: the stored
incremental control law can be applied at a trial parameter without advancing
the accepted load clock, and the same residual and tangent used by SNES can be
evaluated at an arbitrary global unknown vector.  This is the important
architectural distinction: the future bordered XFEM driver can reuse the
production element/material assembly path and only has to add the missing
load/control column and mixed scalar constraint.

The first executable use of that seam is intentionally conservative.  The
driver now accepts a \texttt{bordered-fixed-control} continuation policy that
keeps the protocol parameter fixed at each declared target and routes the
correction through the PETSc bordered backend.  A dedicated regression test
confirms that this adapter closes an elastic \texttt{NonlinearAnalysis} step,
including finite-difference \(r_\lambda\) and external acceptance/commit back
to the model.  The first XFEM smoke is negative evidence rather than a promoted
result: on the bounded-dowel discontinuous branch, pure bordered Newton stalls
before the first small \(1\,\mathrm{mm}\) cyclic target, while SNES Newton--L2
completes the same smoke.  This is a useful localization of the remaining
algorithmic work.  The blocked item is no longer PETSc algebra or access to
the production residual/tangent; it is a bordered line-search and active-set
strategy compatible with the present inconsistent crack-state tangent.

That negative result was then turned into an explicit hybrid runtime policy
rather than hidden behind a looser tolerance.  The executable now accepts
\texttt{bordered-fixed-control-hybrid}.  In this mode the driver first tries
the PETSc bordered correction, but after a configurable streak of bordered
stalls it temporarily skips the bordered attempt and advances the same target
with the selected SNES profile.  The policy therefore behaves like the local
runtime strategy needed by FE\(^2\): attempt the cheaper/reusable correction
when it is productive, fall back to the robust nonlinear profile when the
active crack set makes the bordered direction nonproductive, and record the
number of bordered failures in the manifest.  On the promoted
\(1\times1\times4\), \(z_c=0.60\,\mathrm{m}\), bounded-dowel \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\)
case this hybrid policy preserved the same structural-equivalence gate
\((\mathrm{RMS}_{pk}=0.082,\ |V_b|_{XFEM}/|V_b|_{str}=1.149,\ \sigma_s^{max}
\approx437\,\mathrm{MPa})\), while reducing the pure retry cost from about
\(874\,\mathrm{s}\) to \(256\,\mathrm{s}\).  It is not faster than direct
Newton--L2, but it is now a truthful production-shaped continuation surface:
typed bordered attempt, typed SNES fallback, and explicit diagnostics instead
of silent solver switching.

The next optimization pass moved from solver choice to allocation discipline.
The PETSc bordered kernel now owns a reusable per-solve workspace: one
augmented matrix, one augmented right-hand side, one augmented step vector and
one trial-unknown vector.  These objects are zeroed and reassembled in place
instead of being recreated at every Newton iteration or line-search trial.  The
unit test records this contract through the
\texttt{augmented\_system\_allocations} diagnostic.  This is a small change for
the \(1\times1\times4\) validation model, but it is exactly the kind of change
that matters when many local XFEM sites are solved inside a multiscale step.

A first more-resolved probe was then run with a \(2\times2\times4\) Hex8 XFEM
host up to \(25\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The branch is not promoted as a physical
replacement yet; it is a scaling and diagnostic run.  Newton--L2 with direct LU
completed the probe in about \(46\,\mathrm{s}\).  The hybrid bordered/SNES
route produced the same physical response but took about \(69\,\mathrm{s}\):
the manifest reports six bordered attempts, zero bordered successes, and
eighteen skipped bordered attempts after the adaptive disable policy took over.
A first iterative linear profile, Newton--L2 with GMRES/ILU, failed near the
start of the same probe.  Therefore the immediate scaling conclusion is
conservative but useful: direct LU remains the robust baseline at the current
DOF count, while iterative KSPs need a stronger preconditioning strategy
(field-split or Schur treatment of enriched/interface unknowns, ASM with tuned
subsolves, or AMG only where the operator structure supports it) before they
can be advertised as a scalable replacement.

The guarded mixed-arc run on the promoted \(1\times1\times4\) bounded-dowel
XFEM slice used Newton--L2 and a deliberately moderate target
\(\Delta s_{\mathrm{mix}}=0.50\).  It completed the full \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\)
protocol in \(97.7\,\mathrm{s}\), with \(1851\) accumulated nonlinear
iterations, one rejected observable-arc attempt, exact sampling of the
\(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) drift point and a passed structural equivalence gate:
peak-normalized RMS error \(0.0912\), maximum normalized error \(0.267\),
peak-strength ratio \(1.149\), loop work \(16.16\,\mathrm{MN\,mm}\) versus
\(15.18\,\mathrm{MN\,mm}\) structural, and peak steel stress about
\(437\,\mathrm{MPa}\).  This is slightly more expensive than the direct L2 and
cascade solver-policy runs, so its value is robustness and path auditability,
not raw speed.  A much finer target
\(\Delta s_{\mathrm{mix}}=0.075\) was also tested as a smoke path; it is
valuable diagnostically but oversamples the cyclic loop and is therefore not
promoted for production validation.

The subsequent refinement audit adds negative evidence that is useful before
any larger multiscale run.  A nominal uniform \(1\times1\times6\) host with the
prescribed crack plane \(z_c=0.60\,\mathrm{m}\) is now rejected by the driver,
because that plane coincides exactly with a mesh level of the
\(1.20\,\mathrm{m}\) column and degenerates the shifted-Heaviside split.  A
valid uniform \(1\times1\times5\) mixed-control run does activate the intended
local physics, reaching \(d_{\max}=0.98\) and about \(171\,\mathrm{MPa}\) in the
steel, but it stalls after only \(17.7\,\mathrm{mm}\) of drift and about
\(4143\,\mathrm{s}\) wall time.  This is not evidence against XFEM itself; it
is evidence that the accepted-step SNES continuation route should not be used
for blind refinement.  The next expensive mesh sweep should wait until the real
XFEM residual/tangent/control-column evaluator is connected to the PETSc
bordered mixed-control backend.

The refinement path now also has a cheap local scale audit instead of relying
on intuition or sandbox timeouts.  The header
\texttt{src/validation/ReducedRCLocalMeshScaleAudit.hh} estimates, before model
construction, host elements, nodes, material points, shifted-Heaviside enriched
nodes, explicit-bar DOFs, sparse-matrix memory, nonlinear workspace,
material-state memory, and solver/OpenMP advice.  The XFEM benchmark exposes
that estimate through \texttt{--global-xfem-scale-audit-only}, which writes
\texttt{global\_xfem\_scale\_audit.json} without initializing PETSc.  For the
target \(7\times7\times25\) Hex8-XFEM local mesh, with eight longitudinal bars
and an active crack-crossing bridge, the audit reports approximately \(6000\)
local state DOFs, \(9800\) host material points, \(17.2\,\mathrm{MiB}\)
estimated AIJ matrix storage, and a \(724\,\mathrm{MiB}\) direct-factorization
risk.  The same dry-run separates material-state cost: approximately
\(1.2\,\mathrm{MiB}\) for the elastic proxy, \(7.2\,\mathrm{MiB}\) for the
cyclic crack-band XFEM branch, and \(19.1\,\mathrm{MiB}\) for a Ko--Bathe-like
heavy-reference cost on the same mesh.  The resulting advice is
\texttt{direct\_lu\_reference\_only}: direct LU
is still defensible for isolated reference probes, but the many-site
multiscale route must rely on seed-state caches, Newton warm-start, adaptive
activation of enriched sites, stronger preconditioners, and OpenMP across
independent local sites.  Single-model PETSc \texttt{Mat}/\texttt{Vec}
assembly is intentionally not advertised as OpenMP-parallel until a
thread-safe assembly backend is introduced.

The seed cache is now budgeted rather than implicit.  The local runtime stores
accepted local checkpoints as Newton seeds, but the caller may prescribe
\texttt{max\_cached\_seed\_states}.  When the budget is exceeded, the runtime
evicts inactive, lower-demand and least-recently-used seeds in that order.
Activation also has a lower deactivation threshold, so an enriched local site
does not chatter when the structural demand oscillates around the enrichment
gate.  The multiscale report exposes cached seeds, evictions, checkpoint saves
and restores; these counters are part of the memory/HPC acceptance evidence
before moving from one-way replay to many-site FE2.

The matrix-storage policy is now documented as a checked catalog rather than a
hopeful optimization.  PETSc distinguishes structural/value symmetry and SPD
knowledge through \texttt{MatSetOption}, and the documentation is explicit that
those facts can become unknown again after matrix values change.  Its SBAIJ
creation path stores square blocks in the symmetric-block format, which is only
admissible when the algebraic operator really has that structure.  The current
XFEM local model mixes host displacement DOFs, shifted-Heaviside enrichment,
independent rebar nodes, penalty constraints and crack-bridge active sets; no
current evidence certifies a symmetric positive-definite tangent.  Therefore
\texttt{MATAIJ+LU} remains the correctness reference, while
\texttt{SBAIJ/Cholesky} and \texttt{BAIJ} are guarded candidates.  The promoted
scaling direction is instead general AIJ with physics-aware
\texttt{fieldsplit}, Schur, or ASM preconditioners, because PETSc's
field-split path supports arbitrary index-set splits or \texttt{MATNEST}, and
ASM gives a domain-decomposition route for local blocks.

That ASM route is now executable through the same typed policy surface rather
than through ambient PETSc flags.  The new
\texttt{newton\_l2\_fgmres\_asm} profile uses Newton--L2, \texttt{KSPFGMRES},
\texttt{PCASM}, one-cell overlap and local subdomain solves declared as
\texttt{sub\_ksp=preonly}, \texttt{sub\_pc=lu} under the private
\texttt{falln\_asm\_} options prefix.  This is important architecturally
because the benchmark executable had previously rejected raw PETSc
\texttt{-sub\_*} options at its validation boundary; the subsolver choice now
belongs to the library's solver profile, not to an untracked command-line side
channel.

The same audit is now reproducible as a matrix through
\texttt{scripts/run\_xfem\_scale\_audit\_matrix.py}.  For the cyclic
crack-band XFEM cost branch, the representative sizes are
\[
\begin{array}{c|r|r|r}
\text{mesh} & n_{\mathrm{dof}} & n_{\mathrm{gp}} &
  \text{direct LU risk}~[\mathrm{MiB}]\\
\hline
1\times1\times4  & 204  & 32   & 24.6\\
2\times2\times4  & 309  & 128  & 37.3\\
3\times3\times8  & 744  & 576  & 89.8\\
5\times5\times15 & 2328 & 3000 & 281.0\\
7\times7\times25 & 6000 & 9800 & 724.2
\end{array}
\]
This gives a more disciplined execution order: \(3\times3\times8\) is the next
real cyclic smoke, \(5\times5\times15\) is the first rich reference candidate
once continuation/warm-start is stable, and \(7\times7\times25\) should be
reserved for the local-model gate or for batched FE\(^2\) experiments with
site-level parallel execution.

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.88\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_scale_audit_matrix.png}
  \caption{Dry-run scale audit for the XFEM local-model family.  The figure
  separates state DOFs, material points, and direct factorization risk before
  launching expensive cyclic runs.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-scale-audit-matrix}
\end{figure}

The first consequence of that matrix has already been checked with a real
\(3\times3\times8\) cyclic smoke to \(25\,\mathrm{mm}\), using the promoted
bounded-dowel physics and Newton--L2.  The run completed \(12\) accepted
substeps, \(322\) accumulated Newton iterations, zero failed attempts,
\(d_{\max}=0.98\), peak steel stress about \(218\,\mathrm{MPa}\), and
\(66.7\,\mathrm{s}\) wall time.  This does not promote the mesh as structurally
equivalent; it only confirms that the next local-resolution level is
algorithmically reachable before attempting \(5\times5\times15\) or
\(7\times7\times25\).

The same \(3\times3\times8\) mesh then completed a \(50\,\mathrm{mm}\) smoke in
\(285.7\,\mathrm{s}\).  That run accumulated \(913\) Newton iterations, three
failed attempts recovered by bisection, maximum bisection level \(2\),
\(d_{\max}=0.98\), and peak steel stress about \(375\,\mathrm{MPa}\).  The
interpretation is positive but cautious: the local model remains
axial-balanced and physically coherent, but the amplitude increase already
activates hard steps.  The next amplitude escalation should therefore use
guarded observable continuation or finer adaptive increments, not merely a
larger target drift.

The first typed ASM comparison is intentionally read as a scaling probe, not as
a new physical model.  On the same \(3\times3\times8\) mesh, the
\texttt{FGMRES+ASM+subLU} profile preserved the LU hysteresis almost exactly.
At \(25\,\mathrm{mm}\), both LU and ASM used \(322\) nonlinear iterations; the
wall times were \(66.7\,\mathrm{s}\) and \(68.2\,\mathrm{s}\), respectively.  At
\(50\,\mathrm{mm}\), LU used \(913\) iterations and \(285.7\,\mathrm{s}\),
whereas ASM used \(951\) iterations and \(311.7\,\mathrm{s}\).  Therefore ASM is
not promoted as a faster small-mesh default.  Its value is that it removes the
monolithic global factorization path and creates a checked bridge toward
larger local meshes where the direct-factorization risk, not the sparse matrix
storage itself, dominates memory.

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.84\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_ccb_bounded_dowelx_3x3x8_l2_25mm_probe_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{\(3\times3\times8\) bounded-dowel XFEM cyclic smoke up to
  \(25\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The figure is an algorithmic scaling check, not a
  replacement for the structural-equivalence gate.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-3x3x8-25mm-smoke}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.84\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_ccb_bounded_dowelx_3x3x8_l2_50mm_probe_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{\(3\times3\times8\) bounded-dowel XFEM cyclic smoke up to
  \(50\,\mathrm{mm}\).  The run completes, but hard steps recovered by
  bisection show that the next amplitude increase should use guarded
  continuation.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-3x3x8-50mm-smoke}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.90\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_ccb_bounded_dowelx_3x3x8_linear_solver_probe.png}
  \caption{PETSc linear-solver scaling probe on the \(3\times3\times8\)
  bounded-dowel XFEM branch.  The physical response is unchanged between
  direct LU and \texttt{FGMRES+ASM+subLU}; at this size the iterative route is
  stable but not faster, so it remains a candidate for larger meshes rather
  than the promoted small-mesh default.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-3x3x8-linear-solver-probe}
\end{figure}

Two \(3\times3\times8\) attempts at \(75\,\mathrm{mm}\) are kept as
algorithmic negative evidence: the observable mixed-control run with
\(\Delta s_{\mathrm{mix}}=0.50\) and the fixed-increment Newton--L2 run both
exceeded \(2400\,\mathrm{s}\) without writing a final manifest.  This does not
invalidate the local model; it localizes the current frontier to continuation
strategy and long-run traceability.  The XFEM benchmark therefore now writes
\texttt{global\_xfem\_newton\_progress.csv} incrementally and flushes it after
every accepted point.  If a future long run is stopped by a timeout, the last
accepted drift, reaction, axial balance, steel stress, damage, Newton
iterations, bisection level and residual are still available before the final
manifest exists.

The promoted \(1\times1\times4\) bounded-dowel XFEM branch was then pushed
past the validated \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) closure point to \(250\,\mathrm{mm}\)
and \(300\,\mathrm{mm}\) with the same mixed-control arc-length policy.  Both
runs completed.  The \(300\,\mathrm{mm}\) global XFEM solve accepted 443
protocol points, accumulated 2684 nonlinear iterations, recovered from only
three failed attempts, and reached peak values
\(|V_b|_{\max}=0.0297\,\mathrm{MN}\) and
\(\sigma_{s,\max}=450\,\mathrm{MPa}\).  This is useful stability evidence, but
it is not yet a finite-rotation certificate.  The driver records this contract
explicitly in the manifest: the promoted closure branch is still
\texttt{small-strain}, while \texttt{corotational} is now a real audit branch
of \texttt{ShiftedHeavisideSolidElement}.  The
\texttt{total-lagrangian} and \texttt{updated-lagrangian} routes are now
injected as selectable XFEM paths.  TL uses the
Green--Lagrange strain and the shifted-Heaviside nonlinear material \(B\)
operator in the reference configuration; UL uses Almansi strain, spatial
gradients and current-volume scaling.  The interface no longer hides the
traction measure: the benchmark exposes \texttt{reference-nominal},
\texttt{current-spatial}, and \texttt{audit-dual}.  TL is therefore the first
finite-kinematics path eligible for promotion with reference work, while UL
remains the spatial second-generation path until current-history cyclic audits
are closed.  The
element is parameterized by a
kinematic policy and delegates the enriched bulk operator to
\texttt{src/xfem/ShiftedHeavisideKinematicPolicy.hh}.  That header evaluates
the same shifted-Heaviside slot layout through either a small-strain map or a
corotational map.  The latter extracts a polar frame from the enriched
deformation gradient, filters rigid-body rotation from the bulk strain, rotates
stress and tangent back to the assembly frame, and rotates the cohesive crack
normal with the frozen frame.  The policy seam is intentionally cheap: the
element can pass a slot-provider lambda to the kinematic evaluator instead of
allocating a temporary slot vector at every Gauss point.  Dedicated unit tests
now verify that rigid rotation produces essentially zero corotated,
Green--Lagrange and Almansi strain, while the small-strain path still sees the
expected spurious finite-rotation strain.  The first guarded TL/UL PETSc smoke
runs are deliberately tiny, \(1\times1\times2\) with elastic host material and
\(1\,\mathrm{mm}\) cyclic amplitude.  With the explicit convention, TL with
\texttt{reference-nominal} traction completes, and UL with
\texttt{current-spatial} plus the Nanson-geometric tangent also completes.
This is a plumbing, objectivity and traction-measure checkpoint; full physical
promotion still requires the larger cyclic gates.

The surface-tangent audit is now executable as a separate policy.  The default
mode remains \texttt{frozen-surface-frame}, which keeps the current cheap
Jacobian for production-scale runs.  The intermediate
\texttt{nanson-geometric-surface-frame} mode adds the analytic directional
derivative of \(JF^{-T}N\) and a local normal-traction differential, so it
captures finite surface sensitivity without differentiating the whole element
residual.  On the same \(1\times1\times2\), \(1\,\mathrm{mm}\) elastic smoke,
it completed TL with 18 nonlinear iterations in \(0.91\,\mathrm{s}\), UL with
18 iterations in \(0.90\,\mathrm{s}\), and the corotational branch with 19
iterations in \(0.84\,\mathrm{s}\).  The opt-in
\texttt{finite-difference-surface-frame} mode remains the full oracle: it
differentiates the complete cohesive residual with respect to every local
degree of freedom.  This is important because standard host degrees of freedom
do not contribute directly to the crack jump, but they do change the finite
surface normal and area through the Nanson map.  Dedicated XFEM unit tests
verify both layers: one compares the Nanson surface differential itself
against finite differences of the surface map, and another compares one
standard-DOF column of the TL cohesive tangent against an independent central
finite difference of the cohesive residual.  On the same
\(1\times1\times2\), \(1\,\mathrm{mm}\) elastic smoke, the finite-difference
surface tangent completed TL with 23 nonlinear iterations in
\(3.59\,\mathrm{s}\), UL with 23 iterations in \(3.80\,\mathrm{s}\), and the
corotational branch with 27 iterations in \(4.53\,\mathrm{s}\).  This is too
expensive to be the default for refined meshes, but it is now a precise
regression target for checking the cheaper Nanson-geometric tangent.

The next interface-level correction is now executable as well.  The header
\texttt{ShiftedHeavisideCohesiveKinematics.hh} separates the kinematics of the
cohesive surface from the volumetric strain map.  Small strain keeps the
reference normal and area.  The corotational audit rotates the crack normal
with the polar frame.  TL and UL use Nanson's formula,
\begin{equation}
  n\,\mathrm{d}a =
  J F^{-T}N\,\mathrm{d}A,
  \label{eq:validation-xfem-nanson-cohesive-surface}
\end{equation}
to compute both the current normal and the area scale used by the interface
residual.  This is a real finite-measure improvement over the earlier guard,
and the traction push-forward/pull-back convention is now explicit:
\texttt{reference-nominal} assembles
\(\int_{\Gamma_{c0}}T_0\cdot\delta\left[\!\left[ u \right]\!\right]\,dA\),
\texttt{current-spatial} assembles
\(\int_{\Gamma_c}t\cdot\delta\left[\!\left[ u \right]\!\right]\,da\), and
\texttt{audit-dual} keeps the nominal assembly while reporting the virtual-work
gap between the two measures.  The remaining open item for UL promotion is the
current-configuration cohesive history and large cyclic evidence.

The multiscale start is now represented by a VTK/time-series contract rather
than prose alone.  \texttt{ReducedRCMultiscaleValidationStartCatalog.hh}
declares the fields that must be visible in ParaView over pseudo-time and,
later, physical time: structural curvature and moment, local displacement,
crack opening, cohesive traction, cohesive damage, enriched-DOF norm, steel
stress, and accumulated interface work.  The same catalog fixes the first
multiscale sequence as one-way structural-history replay into XFEM sites,
parallel local-site batches with warm starts, an elastic FE2 smoke, and then a
guarded enriched FE2 one-step smoke.

The executable entry point for that sequence is
\texttt{ReducedRCMultiscaleReplayPlan.hh}.  It does not solve FE2 yet; it
builds an auditable site catalog.  Accepted structural/local hinge history
samples are grouped by candidate site and scored with work-conjugate demand
indicators: curvature, moment, steel stress, damage/localization and
accumulated loop work.  Each site is paired with the
\texttt{ReducedRCLocalMeshScaleAudit.hh} cost estimate and classified as
monitor-only, elastic local control, enriched XFEM replay, or guarded two-way
candidate.  The planner intentionally keeps \texttt{ready\_for\_two\_way\_fe2}
false.  The XFEM driver now writes \texttt{multiscale\_replay\_plan.json} and
\texttt{multiscale\_replay\_site\_catalog.csv}, so the next validation stage is
concrete: replay first, reuse seed states, warm-start Newton, profile local
site batches, and only then enable bidirectional feedback.

The replay catalog is now connected to execution by
\texttt{ReducedRCMultiscaleRuntimePolicy.hh}.  Given an accepted replay plan,
it produces \texttt{LocalSubproblemRuntimeSettings}: bounded seed-cache
capacity, seed restoration, adaptive activation and a serial/OpenMP
site-loop recommendation.  This keeps the first many-site local replay
scientifically traceable: site selection is driven by structural work demand,
while runtime cost is governed by an explicit memory and executor policy.

\texttt{ReducedRCLocalSiteBatchPlan.hh} closes the next scheduling gap.  It
maps selected replay sites into local execution batches, assigns a batch and
slot index to every site, sums the estimated hot-state and direct-factorization
footprints, and declares whether the batch is a direct-LU reference smoke or
requires an iterative AIJ+ASM/field-split path.  The XFEM driver now writes
\texttt{multiscale\_local\_site\_batch\_plan.json} and
\texttt{multiscale\_local\_site\_batch\_plan.csv}; therefore the many-site
replay step has an explicit memory/concurrency schedule before any expensive
PETSc local objects are built.

\texttt{ReducedRCLocalSiteReplayRunner.hh} then supplies the first executable
local-replay loop.  It is solver-agnostic: a local model callback receives the
previous and target structural samples, plus the seed/warm-start intent from
the batch row.  If an increment fails, the runner bisects the structural
history segment up to a declared cutback budget and records accepted steps,
failed attempts, nonlinear iterations, damage, steel stress and replay work.
This is the missing operational layer between planning and FE2: the next
implementation step is to bind this runner to the promoted XFEM local model,
not to invent another selection criterion.

The first benchmark-level use of that runner is intentionally labelled as an
orchestration smoke.  The driver writes
\texttt{multiscale\_local\_site\_replay\_result.json/csv} using a
\texttt{structural\_history\_replay\_oracle} callback, which exercises the
site schedule, replay/cutback bookkeeping, seed and warm-start propagation, and
metric aggregation without pretending that a physical local XFEM solve has
already been performed.  \texttt{ReducedRCMultiscaleReadinessGate.hh} makes
that distinction machine-readable: completed orchestration replay can unlock
the next elastic FE2 wiring smoke, but guarded enriched FE2 remains blocked
until the same runner is bound to the promoted XFEM local model.  This gate is
important scientifically because the transition to multiescala must be based
on work-conjugate local physics, not merely on a successful execution path.

The finite-kinematics contract behind that statement is the following.  The
shifted-Heaviside host displacement is written as
\begin{equation}
  u_h(X)=
  \sum_I N_I(X) u_I
  + \sum_{I\in\mathcal{E}}
    N_I(X)\bigl(H_\phi(X)-H_\phi(X_I)\bigr)a_I ,
  \label{eq:validation-xfem-shifted-heaviside-displacement}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal{E}\) is the set of enriched nodes, \(H_\phi\) is the signed
Heaviside function of the crack level set and \(a_I\) are the enriched jump
unknowns.  The bulk finite-deformation quantity is then assembled from the
same slot layout,
\begin{equation}
  F = I + \nabla_X u_h .
  \label{eq:validation-xfem-f-from-shifted-heaviside}
\end{equation}
Consequently the element does not need separate TL, UL, corotational and
small-strain implementations.  It needs one slot-provider contract and a
kinematic-policy evaluator.  The four policies used in the audit are
\begin{align}
  \varepsilon
    &= \operatorname{sym}(\nabla_X u_h),
  &\text{small strain},\\
  E
    &= \frac{1}{2}\left(F^T F-I\right),
  &\text{total Lagrangian},\\
  e
    &= \frac{1}{2}\left(I-F^{-T}F^{-1}\right),
  &\text{updated Lagrangian},\\
  \hat{\varepsilon}
    &= \operatorname{sym}(R^T F)-I,\qquad F=RU,
  &\text{corotational audit}.
\end{align}
For UL, the gradients used by the linearized spatial operator are
\(\nabla_x N_I=\nabla_X N_I F^{-1}\) and the current-volume scaling is
\(J=\det F\).  For TL, the nonlinear material \(B\)-operator is the directional
derivative of \(E\),
\begin{equation}
  \delta E = B_{\mathrm{TL}}(F)\,\delta d ,
\end{equation}
which is the same finite-deformation linearization used in standard nonlinear
solid FEM references
\cite{BonetWood2008,Crisfield1991_NLFEA_Vol1,Crisfield1997_Vol2,Belytschko2014_NonlinearFEM,MarsdenHughes1994_MathematicalFoundationsOfElasticity}.

This also gives the most compact objectivity regression.  If a quadrature
state undergoes only a rigid rotation \(F=Q\in SO(3)\), then
\(E=0\), \(e=0\) and \(\hat{\varepsilon}=0\).  The small-strain route is
expected to fail that test because
\(\operatorname{sym}(Q-I)\neq0\).  That is exactly what the new
\texttt{shifted\_heaviside\_kinematic\_policy} test enforces: the finite and
corotational policies filter rigid motion, while small strain exposes the
spurious finite-rotation strain.  The same test pins the TL and UL measures
under a uniform axial stretch, so a future refactor cannot silently swap
Green--Lagrange and Almansi semantics.

The reason TL and UL remain guarded is the interface work, not the bulk
operator.  The current cohesive contribution still has the reference-frame
small-displacement form
\begin{equation}
  \delta W_c =
  \int_{\Gamma_{c0}}
    t\bigl(\left[\!\left[ u \right]\!\right]\bigr)\cdot
    \delta\left[\!\left[ u \right]\!\right]\,\mathrm{d}\Gamma_0,
  \qquad
  \left[\!\left[ u \right]\!\right] =
    2\sum_{I\in\mathcal{E}} N_I a_I .
  \label{eq:validation-xfem-cohesive-reference-work}
\end{equation}
For the corotational branch the crack normal can be convected by the frozen
polar frame, \(n_c=Rn_0\), which is sufficient for the present large-rotation
audit.  For TL and UL the implementation now evaluates \(n\,\mathrm{d}a\)
through \eqref{eq:validation-xfem-nanson-cohesive-surface}; additionally, the
Nanson-geometric tangent differentiates the measure analytically and the
finite-difference surface-frame tangent differentiates the whole residual for
diagnostics.  What remains guarded is promotion-quality linearization and
constitutive interpretation of the surface work.  Before promotion, the
Nanson-geometric tangent must be audited on larger cyclic paths against the
finite-difference reference and combined with traction measure, crack-frame
evolution and history variables in work-conjugate measures.  This mirrors the
care required in enriched and discontinuous fracture approximations
\cite{XFEM_Original_Moes1999,XFEM_Moes2000,XFEM_mohammadi2008,XFEM_RCapplication_Yu2018}.

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[
      font=\small,
      box/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, minimum width=2.7cm,
                  minimum height=0.9cm, fill=blue!4},
      guard/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, minimum width=2.7cm,
                    minimum height=0.9cm, fill=orange!10},
      arr/.style={->, thick}
    ]
    \node[box] (driver) at (0,0) {benchmark CLI\\policy token};
    \node[box] (dispatch) at (3.4,0) {compile-time\\dispatcher};
    \node[box] (element) at (6.8,0) {ShiftedHeaviside\\SolidElement};
    \node[box] (slots) at (6.8,-1.55) {slot provider\\\(u_I,a_I,H-H_I\)};
    \node[box] (kin) at (3.4,-1.55) {kinematic\\policy evaluator};
    \node[box] (res) at (0,-1.55) {PETSc residual\\and tangent};
    \node[guard] (guard) at (3.4,-3.05) {TL/UL guard\\manifest + opt-in};
    \draw[arr] (driver) -- (dispatch);
    \draw[arr] (dispatch) -- (element);
    \draw[arr] (element) -- (slots);
    \draw[arr] (slots) -- (kin);
    \draw[arr] (kin) -- (res);
    \draw[arr] (kin) -- (guard);
    \draw[arr] (guard) -- (driver);
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{Policy-injection architecture for the shifted-Heaviside solid.  The
  XFEM element owns the enriched DOF layout and supplies slot data; the
  kinematic policy owns the strain measure and assembly semantics.  TL and UL
  are executable only through an explicit guard until cohesive finite-measure
  work-conjugacy is closed.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-kinematic-policy-architecture}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_smallstrain_large_amplitude_frontier.png}
  \caption{Small-strain promoted XFEM large-amplitude frontier.  The
  \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) point is the structural-equivalence closure point; the
  \(250\,\mathrm{mm}\) and \(300\,\mathrm{mm}\) points are stability/frontier
  evidence under the current small-strain shifted-Heaviside kinematics.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-small-strain-large-amplitude-frontier}
\end{figure}

The first full PETSc/SNES corotational-XFEM run to \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\)
completed on the bounded-dowel \(1\times1\times4\) branch with
mixed-control continuation.  It is a successful finite-rotation audit, but not
yet the promoted replacement for the small-strain closure.  The peak base-shear
ratio is acceptable,
\(|V_b|_{\max}^{xfem}/|V_b|_{\max}^{struct}\approx 1.09\), and the loop work is
close to the structural reference
\((15.36\ \mathrm{MN\,mm}\) versus \(15.18\ \mathrm{MN\,mm})\).  However, the
peak-normalized RMS error is just above the gate
\((0.102>0.10)\), and the maximum normalized error remains too large
\((0.388>0.30)\).  This is the desired kind of negative evidence: the
architecture now injects the kinematic policy without duplicating the element,
and the remaining work is physical calibration and tangent/control refinement,
not hidden plumbing.

The same audit exposed a more local source of finite-rotation bias: the
crack-crossing reinforcement bridge must decide whether its transfer axis is
fixed in the global frame or convected with the host solid.  This is now an
explicit benchmark policy.  The option
\texttt{--global-xfem-crack-crossing-axis-frame corotational-host} rotates the
bridge axis with the host polar frame, while
\texttt{--global-xfem-crack-crossing-host-axis-tangent frozen} preserves the
previous frozen-axis Jacobian.  A second option,
\texttt{finite-difference}, adds a local directional Jacobian for the
host-axis projection.  On the cheap \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\), four-step audit the
two tangent choices produce the same loop
\((|V_b|_{\max}^{xfem}/|V_b|_{\max}^{struct}\approx1.093,\,
e_{RMS}^{norm}\approx0.123,\,
e_{\max}^{norm}\approx0.359)\), but the finite-difference tangent is slower
\((62.3\,\mathrm{s}\) versus \(43.7\,\mathrm{s})\).  Therefore the host-axis
frame remains a physically meaningful corotational extension, whereas the
finite-difference axis tangent is retained as an opt-in diagnostic until it
improves the full-protocol continuation.  The postprocessor was also hardened:
if the global XFEM manifest reports
\texttt{completed\_successfully=false}, the comparison writes
\texttt{status=incomplete\_xfem\_run} and does not evaluate the promotion
gate.

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.92\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_ccb_bounded_dowelx_nz4_corotational_mixed_arc_200mm_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{First full corotational-XFEM audit to \(200\,\mathrm{mm}\) on the
  bounded-dowel local model.  The branch filters rigid rotations through the
  shifted-Heaviside kinematic policy seam and runs to completion, but it is not
  yet promoted because the RMS and maximum-error gates are not both satisfied.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-corotational-200mm-audit}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure}[htbp]
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=0.90\textwidth]{figures/validation_reboot/xfem_mixed_arc_length_l2_arc050_guarded_vs_structural_200mm_hysteresis.png}
  \caption{Guarded mixed-control arc-length continuation on the promoted
  bounded-dowel XFEM local model.  The driver keeps all declared reversal
  points, rejects overly long observable jumps and preserves the structural
  hysteresis gate.  The price is additional nonlinear work relative to direct
  Newton--L2; the benefit is a continuation seam suitable for multiscale
  checkpoint/restart.}
  \label{fig:validation-reboot-xfem-mixed-arc-guarded-200mm}
\end{figure}

Architecturally, that future step is now also tied back to the generic local
subproblem contract in \texttt{src/analysis/SubscaleModelConcepts.hh}. A future
enriched local model should not enter the library as ``just another element''.
It should enter as a local-model family that still answers the same abstract
questions as the current baseline:
\begin{equation}
  \left(
    \text{driving state},
    \text{effective operator},
    \text{checkpoint},
    \text{taxonomy}
  \right),
\end{equation}
even if its internal discretization changes from standard continuum to XFEM or
DG/HDG. This is what keeps validation artifacts, multiscale orchestration and a
future Python/Julia wrapper from being rewritten every time a new local family
is introduced.

The important methodological conclusion is still conservative, but it has now
changed sign. The evidence no longer supports keeping the standard smeared
continuum as the physical multiscale local model for this benchmark; it should
remain the cheaper regression/control branch.  The promoted physical local
baseline is the bounded-dowel XFEM branch, because it is the first continuum
resolution model that reproduces the structural cyclic loop within the
predefined quantitative gate.  This is not a claim that the final production
model is complete.  Following the same spirit as the
Spiliopoulos--Lykidis methodology \cite{SpiliopoulosLykidis2006}, the next
step is to stabilize the 3D solid + embedded/enriched reinforcement baseline,
its loading/unloading strategy, tangent policy and computational contract
before using it inside a large multiscale dynamic simulation. What the library
now has is not a speculative new element, but a promoted enriched local-model
family and an explicit seam through which future XFEM/DG variants can enter
without rewriting the validation program or the multiscale orchestration.

\section{The first coding artifact of the reboot}

The catalog itself is meant to stay lightweight and outside the hot numerical
path:

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++,caption={Representative compile-time contract for the rebooted validation campaign.},label={lst:validation-reboot-catalog}]
constexpr auto plan = fall_n::canonical_validation_reboot_workstream_table_v;

static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_validation_workstream_priority_count_v<
        fall_n::ValidationWorkstreamPriorityKind::mandatory_blocker> == 8);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_validation_reference_structural_column_gate_count_v == 5);
static_assert(
    fall_n::canonical_validation_reference_continuum_column_gate_count_v == 7);
\end{lstlisting}

\section{Immediate execution policy}

The immediate execution policy of this reboot is therefore:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item stabilize the methodological baseline;
  \item validate the reduced-order rectangular RC column first;
  \item build the equivalent continuum column second;
  \item compare both routes quantitatively;
  \item only then reopen walls, frames, subassemblages, FE\textsuperscript{2},
    and building-scale simulations as normative validation targets.
\end{enumerate}

This is narrower than the current ambition of the repository, but also more
scientifically defensible.  That tradeoff is intentional.
